<Author>MrsCLondonUK
<Content>Not so Majestic I stayed at this hotel for a week with my husband over Christmas/New Year. We booked for 6 nights at 219 Euros per night. The room we were originally allocated was very small with limited facilities (no mini bar; CD player; DVD) and certainly not worth the money. There was an awful sewage smell along the corridor and in the room. We complained immediately. The manager was slow to respond at first but after we told the staff that we were thinking of moving to a different hotel they were, unsurprisingly, very helpful. We were moved to a bigger, more fragrant room, on the second floor which was much better and we were not charged any additional amount which was good. When my husband booked with the hotel he was advised that there was a CD player in each room. This is not correct. Howeevr, we were offered the loan of a CD player at a cost of 30 Euros per day - outrageous! The service generally was far below the standard I would expect of a 5 star hotel. We consider ourselves to be pretty laid back (especially on holiday) but we found that we were constantly having to chase reception/housekeeping as they were very slow in responding to our requests. It took three days to get an answer back about the CD player. The other thing we were disappointed by is that breakfast was not included in our room rate but quite frankly I would recommend going outside the hotel for breakfast as it was not worth the 25 Euros the hotel were charging for it. I have to say we were very pleased with the gym and the roof terrace and views over Barcelona are great and I imagine this would be fantastic in the summer. There is also a great spa - if a little costly. The location of the hotel is also good with great access to main sites, shopping areas and some excellent restaurants. We are accustomed to staying in smaller boutique hotels with excellent service levels (e.g. Ca Maria Adele (Venice); Carlisle Bay (Antigua); The W (New York); Hotel Du Vin (UK); Tokoriki (Fiji)) so this was very different experience for us. Some may like it - particularly the mature conservative crowd - but this not a hotel from the young (or, as in our case, the young at heart) for whom service levels are important. Not to mention contemporary styling (did I mention that the hotel is quite traditional). For those PLUs (people like us), I would suggest looking at Hotel Neri and Hotel Arts (which houses has the fantastic Arola restaurant).Mr and Mrs C

<Content>perfect location We just returned from 3 weeks in europe. we had heard and read mixed reviews about the hotel majestic. we decided that the location on the passeig de gracia was perfect. right in the center more or less of everything. roughly a 10 minute walk to the gothic quarter, less than 10 minutes to the start of las ramblas, 5 minutes to the turistic bus lines that take you everywhere. bars restaurants everywhere. we reserved a superior room and found it to more than adequate. i am claustrophobic and had no problem. the bathroom was modern with ample counter space. the floors were quiet although we were there thru a weekend and it was hectic on the street until 3-4 am. the price one pays to be so close to everything. the staff was friendly and helpful but we found thru out the area that catalun or spanish is really all most anyone of the locals speak. at many of the attractions there is some people who are fluently bilingual. we loved the city enjoyed the hotel accomodations and found what ever we needed they were willing to help. communications never were a problem just a bit interesting. definetly intend to go back.

<Author>TaylorPeat
<Content>Not Good I was very much looking forward to my stay at the 'five star 'Hotel Majestic but from the minute I arrived I was underwhelmed. I booked directly with the hotel and paid extra for a room with a balcony. The room itself was fine, nothing special but fine, however when I went out on the balcony I was extremely disappointed. Not only was it shabby and a little bit grubby looking but there were these awful large bolts and screws exposed all along the wall, which not only looked unsightly but could also have easily caused a nasty scrape. We informed reception who came and had a look at the exposed bolts but didn't actually offer to do anything about them. The hotel's roof top terrace is tiny and only has about 7 or 8 sun loungers so unless you are up there first thing in the morning you can forget about it. The final straw came when I requested an additional sun lounger for our private balcony (as there was only one on it). The girl at reception reluctantly agreed to check 'if it was possible' and said she would call me back to let me know. I sat waiting for 30 mins with no repsonse. At this stage I had had enough. So we packed our bags, checked out and went to another hotel. When we were checking out they did apologise and offered to upgrade us to a suite but by that stage I just wanted to get out of there. However they did charge us for the one night we stayed. It is possible that we were just unlucky with the room we were given but overall I expect alot more from a 5 star standard hotel. The atmosphere in the hotel is pretty stade and the staff are not the friendliest. I wouldn't recommend this hotel.

We finally complained to the lady at Guest Relations ( very pleasant and concerned) and she managed to get us the use of a standard ( very small) room for our last day..she also refunded the cost of 1 night 's bed and breakfast for the poor service we had received.The hotel has a great location but the staff, mostly men, seem really miserable and arrogant and most of the rooms ( public areas as well) are small and have no natural light.

<Author>asloan2348
<Content>This should not be a five star hotel We have just returned from a three day stay in Barcelona.We stayed in a standard room at a cost of 拢198 per day - room only. The smallest five star hotel room in the world? Certainly the smallest that I have ever been in. I've never had the desire to swing a cat but I couldn't have done it in that room.The air conditioning did not work properly. As a result, we had to sleep with the window open and as we faced one of the busiest streets in the city it did not make for a relaxing night.The bathroom was the crowning glory. It was almost impossible to stand up to pee as the pan was so close to the sink. It was also pretty difficult to sit down as I struggled to get my feet on the floor between the pan and the sink. The shower had all of the power of a left handed serve from a right handed tennis player - which was just as well because there was no shower screen which then meant that the floor and the toilet pan were soaked every time the shower was used.From the smell between the lift and the room door, I think that there is a dead body somewhere on floor eight.The basement restaurant looked plastic and soul less - we gave it a body swerve.The only reason that my review stretches to two stars was that we ate at Restaurant Drolma. We had the menu exclusive which was wonderful - albeit at a price - dinner for two with an OK bottle of Rioja and a couple of glasses of champagne came to a whopping 485 Euros.Barcelona was superb. Drolma was superb. The Majestic was a massive disappointment.

<Author>calcalino
<Content>A hotel way past its best This hotel is living in the past and on its former reputation.The reception staff are surly and unhelpful, the barmen lazy and uninterested in their work. An aroma of cigar smoke drifts into the lounge from the enclosed cigar bar. There is no daylight in the public areas except in the foyer. The pool is closed for refurbishment. (we were there in March/April 2008... don't know when it will re-open).And the bedrooms -an utter disaster, unless you take into account the bed linen and the night time chamber maid service (which was not to be relied on).The size of our bedroom did not merit a deluxe rating. It would have been more suited to as Travel Lodge or motel - so much so that we had to ask the hotel to remove some of the furniture in order to accommodate all our luggage.We had booked an upgraded room only to find that the city view was out of a window that was positioned almost above our heads and what we could see comprised sky and aerials. After complaining, they showed us other rooms, either with no window (a deluxe rating!!!), or dormer windows or again tiny. Finally we had no choice but to accept what they offered - exactly what they'd shown us in the first instance. It was overpriced, very small and not at all acceptable. By way of 'apology' (?) we were given a bowl of fruit in our room and a bottle of cheap cava. This is no way compensated for the price we had paid and the expectations we had of top class accommodation.All I can say is that despite its excellent location, the hotel does not treat its guests in the manner one would expect from a deluxehotel.Loved Barcelona, but will never stay in the Majestic again.

<Author>kolinsky
<Content>Fantastic location Just got back from a '3 for the price of 2' night stay at the Majestic Hotel, Barcelona. Before we even got in the hotel we were greeted by the doormaen and our luggage was promptly taken to reception for us, where check in was quick. Despite being hours early we were shown to our room. The location is perfect. Right in the centre of all the sight seeing but also in a part of the city that is more upmarket, so you feel safer at night.  The room was huge and the bathroom luxurious. Air con and heating controls were in the room, safe, mini bar, work station, TV and all the little extras you would expect. Bathrobes and slippers were provided. The bed was very comfortable as were the pillows. Breakfast was superb. One of the best selections I've encountered. Fresh fruit, cereals, pastries, breads, hams, cheeses, bacon, eggs, pancakes, tortilla and fresh coffee. Throughout the hotel we found the staff to be extremely helpful, polite and professional. The hotel was clean, quiet and had a relaxing atmosphere, which is appreciated after a days walking and sight seeing. Didn't use the pool because the weather was to cold. The only fault I can find is that there was a few cracked tiles in the bathroom, but that's me being really picky. Will use this hotel on our next visit.

<Author>Valerie_UK
<Content>Doesn't Deserve It's Five-Star Rating. I am not someone who usually complains, but the Hotel Majestic managed to defeat even my stoic British spirit.Upon arrival, we were ignored as we repeatedly tried to get the receptionist's attention.When we were finally shown to our room on the seventh floor, it was dark, dingy, and slightly dirty in parts. The small window was directly opposite another room's window, which was a mere two metres away, and allowed minimal light through as our view was blocked by walls, drain pipes and gutters. The walls were extremely thin, meaning we could hear every noise the rather passionate couple next door to us were making.The toiletries brought my partner out in a rash, and the bathrobes were so coarse they aggravated my eczema. Our shower kept switching between scalding hot and freezing cold, and the lavatory kept blocking. We had requested a double room, but were met with two (fairly lumpy) single beds. We were told to merely 'push the beds together', and deal with it. Had I not paid over 拢200 a night, I probably wouldn't have minded so much, but as it was, it didn't seem appropriate 5 -Star behaviour.The final icing on the -frankly, rather rotten- cake was that the pool and sun terrace were closed. With such a major part of the hotel out of service, one would expect there to be some notification on the website, and to be reminded of this at check in. However, I have scoured the website and found no such notification, and was certainly not notified of it at reception. Instead, guests are informed of the pool's closure via a small, slightly dog-eared sign in the elevators.My advice to any potential guests of the hotel majestic is this-DON'T LET YOUR HOLIDAY BE RUINED - FIND SOMEWHERE ELSE!!!

<Content>Very disappointed with this hotel Have just returned from a celebration break away to The 5* Majestic Hotel. We had booked for 3 nights but only stayed the one as it was so terrible. After complaining to reception, who were very cold and unsympathetic, gave us a couple of free passes for a pool 3 blocks away (hardly the same!). Our room was nothing like you would expect either from a 5* hotel, plus we had booked a superior room. The bathroom was the smallest I have ever seen. We chose to check out the following morning and find a hotel that met with our requirements and luckily we found Hotel 1898 which I must say, was a lovely hotel, and only 4 star, but in my opinion far superior to the Majestic. We felt we were then able to finally enjoy our break away. On returning home I wrote a letter to the GM as I feel very strongly that they should be advising all potential customers of the fact that their facilities are closed due to refurbishment, thus giving people the option especially as they pride themselves on their 'main priority being Customer Satisfaction'. I wanted answers as to why we were not advised in the first place, but he basically avoided all of my questions, so again, I wrote to him, only to receive another letter back stating that they are improving their facilities. I found the whole experience totally appalling, how we were treated beforehand, during and after our stay. I never normally complain, but on this occassion I felt i had too. its not about the money (although it did cost us around 240 euros for experience) but the fact that people like ourselves were able to book this hotel under false advertising.

<Author>Sigrid66
<Content>Just go. I am dutch mum of 3 young boys. Since i really needed a break alone, my husband offered me a weekend Barcelona to do some serious sightseeing (GHAUDI!!) and even more serious shopping!I chose the Majestic based on its location, and for the fact the manager of the hotel actually made the effort to read Tripadvisor and react to negative comments. I always read everything on tripadvisor before booking any hotel or holiday as i find it the best revieuw site worldwide. This is however my first written revieuw!I booked a single classic room. Basically I paid as much as a doubleroom would cost but i still expected to get the smallest room around really. NOT true. I got a nice room, quit spacious with a large bathroom (room 242). I originally was given another room but asked if i could smoke there and that was not the case so i was given another. I must say, walking thru the hallways and seeing other rooms being cleaned, that they seemed smaller. So yes, the rooms may not be big bit its a very old building, rooms differe in size and I did book the cheapest category. So if you take a classic room then indeed you have NO vieuw, and a smaller room. I had no vieuw indeed but i did not care and did not expect it. Its not like I'd go to barcelona to look out of the window all day, is it?Now for the Hotel. I loved it. Its peacefull, classy but very friendly. I never felt out of place there tho i strolled around in jeans and Tshirt basically and i clearly look like a tired mum and not like a potential Armani customer (Armani is next door). Everybody was friendly and willing to help or answer my questions.The Hotel is very clean, looks very wel maintained and is nicely decorated. The beds are comfortable, nice big towels, slippers, TV with several ebglish spoken channels etc. Only the bathrobes.....they are kidsizes. If you are over size 14, bring your own:P That goes for the whole of Barcelona tho, loads of shops but not a chance of buying any clothing over size M (14 or so). So I shopped a lot for my kids and saved my husband some money.Breakfast is standard buffet, not many fancy things but sufficient. The breakfast restaurant is maybe the nly area of ther hotel i did not like much, its in the basement and it does not have much atmosphere. It does the trick tho, you can sit comfortably and eat enuff to last till dinner.Negatives?Hotelwise i cant think of any that would not make me look utterly picky. Servicewise, only one thing botherred me. I do not use a creditcard. I dont have one, i hate them. I pay with my bankcard in Holland and cash elsewhere. My husband obviously has some but they are in his name so i dont take them. Even tho my hotel was payed for already they wanted my creditcard at check in. I said i didnot have one. I got the weirdest look ever, as if i am a total moron for not having one. Then I had to deposit 50 euros a night, apperantly to cover damage or costs i would cause or make before running of...or so....I basically felt like a criminal and told the guy i didnot think it was nice to display so much distrust on a guest, who already payed for her whole stay. He just shrugged. I payed the 100 euros (2 nights). When I checked out 2 days later there was another receptionist. I asked for my money back and he asked for a receipt. I never got one when i checked in and told him that. He shaked his head, started looking in the computer for a while and eventually gave me the money back. Now that made me feel a bit weird, but other than that..i loved it there. If you have doubts, just book it, location is superb, service was great as well, apart from the little incident above.Please note the swimmingpool and spa are being rebuild and are not done till about may this year. Enjoy!

<Author>Scottie001
<Content>Great Location We stayed three nights in January. The room was somewhat small; however, we had a choice in the category of a suite or a room facing the Passeig de Gracia, and we opted for the view. We made the right choice, as the room had french doors to a small patio with a tremendous view. Everything else about the room was good - clean, nice bathroom, etc. We were only there a few nights, and who spends a lot of time in the room? Our reservation did not include breakfast, but there are plenty of options close by. There is a coffee/pastry house just across the street. The location was terrific - close to public transportation, shops, restaurants, etc. Service in the hotel was good, with easily-available advise which was appreciated. Good dinner options around. I would recommend Costa Gallega, one block north on the Passeig de Gracia (get the piquillo peppers stuffed with crabmeat, patatas bravas, and wash down with a good cold glass of the local Penedes wine - Vina Sol. Very reasonable. Oh yes, I forgot, the beds were about the most comfortable we ever slept in. I would definitely recommend this hotel.

<Author>ElNorEast
<Content>Hotel Majestic - A Mixed Bag. Stayed at the Hotel Majestic for a week in late November, booked as a 5-star choice from a list of conference hotels. As there were three of us staying in one room (married couple and a sister), we inquired in advance if it would be possible to get a triple room, which they were happy to arrange for us at a supplement of 50 Euros / night + 10 Euros / night required breakfast charge. The kind woman in the sales department who helped us with this request was lovely and could not be faulted.Upon arrival we were taken to a tiny smoking room with a sofabed pulled out. The foot of the sofa bed rested against the foot of the double bed (more on that later). Having informed the hotel in advance that I am six months pregnant, I found their choice to put us in a smoking room odd and after asking politely they moved us up one floor to a similarly tiny room, with dirty scuffed walls and grubby carpet. The furnishings were something you would expect to find in a Holiday Inn (I am serious). The room was certainly not five star and we asked to be moved again - this time a bellman was involved, and he steered us to a suitable room. Bellmen and housekeepers always know the nicest rooms in hotels, so take their advice!Once we were finally ensconced in our room (paying ANOTHER 30 Euros a day for an upgrade to a superior room) we started to notice some interesting trends amongst the staff. This is a hotel where the staff are quite convinced that they are better than their guests - if you are not wearing a fur coat and Blahniks, you may as well be crawling out of the gutter. Doors were not opened for us by the doorman, we were eyeballed with disdain by the guys who stand on the stairs (security?), and I once saw a front desk clerk (they are all men who are 40 years +) look up at my sister - a really stunning redhead - and shake his head. We were wearing very normal clothes: black trousers, black shoes (no tennis shoes), cashmere sweaters and the like. Being pregnant, my clothes certainly weren't Chanel but I wasn't turned away from any restaurant in the city, so I figured I looked OK. We had worn the same basic outfits for a week at the Hotel Imperial in Vienna, which was a MUCH nicer hotel, so I think it must have been a Hotel Majestic trademark to make the guests feel uncomfortable.One afternoon my sister and I (we are 29 yo and 39 yo) wandered into the lobby bar for some coffee and a light lunch. The blond model-like bar attendant took our order, brought it to us and then disappeared. As we were halfway through eating our pizza, another bar worker came through and put up menus for an afternoon tea they had been serving for an hour, something that the model man had neglected to tell us about. We were never offered refills, checked on, anything, and when we finally got the server to give us our check we asked if we could put it on our room he threw his pen down on the table and walked off in a huff. Breakfast was dull and we only went once, despite being forced to pay an obligatory 10 euros a day per person for it. It's held in a windowless conference room in the basement. Every couple of minutes the room shakes from the Metro that runs right by the hotel. The staff were uninterested and unfriendly, and the food was very dull - pastries came from huge catering packs, etc.However, the thing that makes me really cringe about this hotel, the thing that cemented in my mind NEVER AGAIN, was the bed situation. We booked a double room. We saw three of them. Apparently, to the Hotel Majestic, a double bed is two twins made separately and then pushed together with a small blanket at the bottom. They make their beds by putting on the bottom sheet, then the top sheet, blanket, another top sheet, and then tucking the entire affair under the mattress. Anyone who has stayed in a hotel where this is the common practice knows that when you untuck your bed to get into it the bottom sheet comes out as well, and unless you really want to slide around all night you have to re-tuck the bottom sheet in. Imagine now that you are staying with your husband / wife / signficant other, and you have to separate the beds (they are on rollers), untuck the beds completely, retuck in the bottom sheets for both beds, then push the beds back together. There is no interaction between parties in the separate beds, because you will fall through the crack between the beds (made especially dangerous since the beds are on rollers). EVERY NIGHT FOR A WEEK I went through this bedtime routine; I have stayed in many hotels where there are twins pushed together for a double bed, but they ALWAYS make the bed as ONE bed, not two separate beds pushed together. It was absolutely infuriating, ridiculous and completely stupid for a five-star hotel. Aside from this huge flaw, the housekeeping was very good.However, after a week of being completely frustrated by what I perceived to be a lower-range Westin or even Sheraton, I discovered something that really made me laugh - they do roaring cruise trade!! As I waited on a sofa by the elevators on my (thankfully) last day, I saw streams of cruisers walking by, all dressed in cruise wear, all much more poorly dressed than we were and much less travel savvy. It made me smile to think that all these obviously high-class Barcelona hotel clerks and bar waiters had to deal with these people all the time, and what a strain it must be for them to have to lower themselves to actually speaking with such riff raff!My advice: stay somewhere else. The location is OK, but not great; the staff are generally pretty much up themselves and what should be a welcoming comfortable place winds up making you wish you were somewhere else. Avoid.  
<Date>Dec 3, 2007

<Author>bembridge
<Content>It is okay, but not great for a 5 star This was actually the 2nd time I have stayed at the Hotel Majestic in Barcelona. The first was about 3 or 4 years ago on a long weekend break. This time I was here for work.I cannot work out if I like it or not, and probably overall am indifferent and think there are much better hotels offering better value and service in the city.On the plus side, it has a great location right in the centre of the upmarket shopping area on a very wide and attractive boulevard. In addition to shops there are many great restaurants as well as being near to attractions like a Gaudi museum. There is a small but attractive roof terrace with pool with great views (closed for renovation until about April 2008).The rooms are very varied in size. This trip I had a large room which was very quiet as at the back of the hotel and not overlooking the main road. The air-conditioning is very quiet which is a boon as I hate air-conditioning noise and in most hotels have to switch it off at night no matter how hot or cold it gets!The rooms feel dated and uninspired decor wise, although they are not shabby at all. The bed and pillows were very comfortable and this combined with the quiet made for a great night sleep.There are some strange things like very limited cupboard space and no easy access to a plug for your PC (at the desk you have to reach behind the desk to try and get a plug in).The food is ok but nothing unusual.If I had a choice of coming back here or staying somewhere else for the price (as it is a 5 star), I would chose somewhere else.

<Author>suzy39
<Content>Quite simply a fabulous hotel Stayed at the majestic for three nights in November. I was concerned after reading the reviews about this hotel but all that I can say is that I had absolutely no complaints about this hotel. For it to be ranked 50 on tripadvisor is a serious error - it should be in the top 5. Our room was a superior twin room and was bigger than some hotel rooms I have stayed in in Europe. ALL the staff were a credit to the hotel; in particular Tim at reception and the lady at concierge who both gave us fabulous recommendations for dinner each evening.(if you are looking contempary catalan food try the Windsor - the food was exquisite). Nothing was too much trouble for the staff in this hotel. During our stay the hotel's pool was under reconstruction and will be until April 2008 so if pools are a must for your holiday be aware - they were not for us so we did not care about this. Whilst this is a 5 star hotel it thankfully did not have the overbearing pomp and ceremony that some 5 star hotels have (which was a very welcome relief!!) and you did not feel self conscience when walking through the hotel in jeans and t-shirts. Special word of thanks to the Manager Bruno - every email I sent was answered promptly and the hotel went out of their way to beat the prices that I had been quoted on various internet sites. The cava and fruit basket were truly appreciated. I would not hesitate at all to stay in this hotel as it was quite simply fabulous.

<Author>JB_Parrothead
<Content>Not even close to 5 star service This hotel has plenty to offer but falls short on many levels. Our situation was a problem for them from the beginning. The issue---we were 3 adult travelers seeking 1 room. I contacted the hotel via e-mail to request our options. The only single room option was to book a junior suite, which was 400 euros per night plus 50 euros for the extra person. So that is what I booked.We stayed 3 nights. The problem was room service and housekeeping never got their act together and provided accommodations for 3 people. We had 2 of everything from drink glasses to bath towels to bath robes to sets of bed pillows. We kept asking for more supplies, including the shampoos and each time they would bring them but the next day it went back to 2 of everything. Finally I went down to the lobby and demanded management fix the problem. The lobby manager told me to return to my room and tell housekeeping what I wanted. I told him that he should deal with housekeeping, not me. I find this unbelievable in a 5 star hotel and told him that loud and clear.Other problems we encountered were the extra bed never had the same feather pillows the king bed had; other rooms had white bath robes and black pool robes--ours only had 2 white ones; the extra bed for the first 2 nights was actually just the sofa which they made up as a bed but there was no mattress pad, just a sheet over the sofa seat; the extra bed linens were only 2 sheets, no blanket was supplied and the pillow was a 12 square throw pillow with a case on it; one day the sofa was made up as a bed all day long rather than making it up that way only in the evening so we had no place to watch TV or visit; every night only 2 of the 3 beds got turn down service. It was basically the poorest 5 star service I have ever received.There were some good things about this hotel. The location was perfect, right in the middle of things yet off The Ramblas, which all 3 of us preferred. The rooftop bar and swimming pool were both wonderful. Every night we went up to the roof for drinks and music, the view was a great end to a long day of trekking all over BCN. The breakfast was among the best we had anywhere in Spain.I realize we would not have had these problems if we were 2 to a room, but they did take our extra 50 euros and they did agree that 3 could be accommodated in 1 room so I fault the hotel entirely. The manager did give us an additional free standard room on our 3rd night, but I had to insist she do something more than her first offer which was a free breakfast on our last day. This negotiation took an hour, in the US it would have been a given. At no time did I get the impression that management would do almost anything to make it right--both managers I dealt with were really not interested in going above and beyond to assure our stay was a good one.

<Author>jbtexas
<Content>Very good location, very comfortable hotel The Majestic is a very comfortable, upscale hotel located in the center of Barcelona's shopping district on the Passeig de Gracia. As such, the location puts you right in the center of shopping action, a six block walk to Placa de Catalunya, two blocks from Gaudi's Casa Mila and two blocks from a metro station and Turistic bus stop (both north and south routes). This makes the location hard to beat, and is away from the noise of Las Ramblas (Rambla de Catalunya is a block away, but it is much quieter than Las Ramblas from Placa de Catalunya to the coast). If you want a hotel central to it all, but yet away from the tourist crowds of Las Ramblas or Barri Gotic, this hotel is hard to beat.We also found the hotel rooms quite comfortable and have absolutely no complaints about our four night stay there. We arrived at the hotel after our overnight flight from the US at 9:30 am and were able to get right into our room. I don't know if this is the norm, but we were sure pleased with this! Our room was #646, which was one price notch above a standard room. We found the room very comfortable with everything in good working order. Only two small minor observations about the room. If there was a clock, we could not find it. I realize that most European hotels don't have table top clocks a la American hotels, but for a hotel in this price range, I would have expected something. Also, there were no facial wash cloths. Again, very typical for Europe, but again at this price point, I was a bit disappointed. Our room was an interior room, so we had no view, but we also heard no outside noise. From the evacuation chart on the door of the room, it appears that rooms vary considerably in size. If you want a large room, I'd suggest calling the hotel direct to make a reservation. Further, if you look very closely at the hotel photos on the hotel web site, you will see that the floors are not level. You will climb up and down sets of steps as you go from one end of the floor to the other (there are two separate elevator banks - one on the Passeig de Gracia side, and one half way down the Valencia side). If you are staying at the hotel on a US dollar bankrolled vacation, you may wish to think twice about dining at the in-house acclaimed Drolma restaurant. Even without wine, your bill will approach or exceed $300. The food was fine, and the service attentive, if a bit rushed, but for $300, I would be hard pressed to say it was worth it. If your home currency is anything other than the US dollar, I'd recommend the restaurant.The hotel has a rooftop lounge / lap pool / deck area. There are much better places to get an elevated view of Barcelona (Castell Montjuic, Tibidabo, Parc Guell for starters), but it is a pleasant place to relax. If you want to save a few euros (and for US visitors, you'll need to!), rather than patronizing the hotel restaurant (Condial) for breakfast, you may want to consider Fresh  Ready, a small cafe a block and a half south on Passeig de Gracia. You can get cereal, fruit, pastries and coffee / tea and then sit out on sidewalk tables watching people go to work - not a bad way to start a vacation day! Fresh  Ready is open all day, and sitting at a sidewalk table with a sandwich / salad / beverage makes for some great people watching.  
<Date>Sep 22, 2007

<Author>tempcooler
<Content>Pleasant Stay We stayed in the Hotel Majestic for 3 nights in August. The location is great, on a beautiful tree lined block in the center of the shopping district, close to several Gaudi buildings and walkable to La Rambla. We got a pretty good 3 nights for the price of 2 deal via the hotel website. The service was quite good. Attentive, spoke good English. The rooms are clean and nice, and size wise about what we expected (smallish, about average by European standards). We got the superior room that added a small sitting area which probably was worth it to make the room feel a bit more spacious. The internet service is very expensive which was a drawback. The room had a funny smell each time after it was cleaned. We got used to it after a while, but it was weird. The main lobby was undergoing renovation and the temp lobby is small and can get crowded. Overall it was a nice stay. You have to be realistic with what you can get for your money in Barcelona and while the Majestic was not super luxurious it was comfortable and upscale.

It was 310, a twin bedded room in the back overlooking a parking lot and some air-conditioning unit. The front desk said it was a quiet room with lots of light. We demurred and insisted on a different room (and overheard others get upgrades at front desk) - and so we ended up in 729, with a balcony in front of hotel and a lovely view of Passeig de Gracia. Nice, light, quiet enough despite vehicle traffic outside.It was a somewhat painful time-consuming process to obtain an okay room. The room was smallish, bathroom functional but stonework in need of sprucing up. Mattress in need of replacement or rotation - I felt I would slide off the bed because the mattress leaned towards the telephone. Bedding okay - sheets decent enough quality. Plenty of pillows of different shapes and hardness. Message light on phone stayed lit for entire stay despite our numerous calls to front desk to address it. Housekeeping excellent. Hard finding any English speaking TV stations on the lovely flat screen TV. Turn down service nice touch. No noise from hallway.Elevators (all sets of them)- pathetically slow, at times, and small and hot. Hotel lobby and fancy restaurant undergoing some sort of renovation (someone said the air conditioning system was being fixed). Breakfast (included in price) was served in a conference room on lobby level our first 3 days and then in usual location (sub-basement level) last two days. Nice buffet selection...attentive service. No complaints. Free newspapers (some in English).The hotel has a decent gym area near the pool on roof as well as sauna and steam room. The sauna and steam can be used only upon payment of fee and with reservation. Plenty of chaises and chairs on roof, from which you can see Sagrada Familia Church, port, Montjuic- etc etc. Great views.The hotel is less than one block from Passeig de Gracia metro station which is very convenient to get down to Ramblas or to Barciloneta (sic) or anywhere. We took a Renfe train from that station to Sitges this past Sunday. Hotel is okay walk (slightly downhill) to Placa Catalon, but you'll will find the slight street grade incline makes the return walk a bit more grueling. Hotel was longer walk from Placa Catalon than we would have liked.Free ice and lemon and lime flavored water available 24/7 off lobby, along with red and green apples.Concierge extremely gracious and generous with time, advice, restaurant recommendations and reservations. Last night, we had ballet tickets at Liceu and had to depart hotel before Cafe d'Academia opened and could confirm. We headed for the popular restaurant after our show ended and, sure enough, hotel had come through with sought after reservation. Kudos to Concierge Christine and her colleagues.Despite its many features, I would be inclined to stay in a hotel in the Barri Gotic next time or, much more likely, the fabulous Hotel Arts right on the beachfront in Port Olympic, but a five minute walk from old city. We toured that hotel, and the rooms and views are impressive.I feel we got our money's worth at the Majestic, but only because we landed a terrific internet rate.

<Author>Momomax
<Content>Great location; Disappointing service We booked this hotel for 4 nights prior to a cruise based on Trip Advisor recommendations. We had high hopes, given that it seems to be rated at least a 4-star hotel. I don't have comparisons, as I have never stayed in Barcelona before, but I would rate this hotel as no better than a Hilton in the U.S.The staff were helpful on restaurant recommendations, but otherwise indifferent. Our room was adequate/small and would have been quiet (even though facing the main street) except for a party with children in the next room who stayed up until 2:00 am every night screaming. I finally had to personally ask them to pipe the kids down. The hotel could not change our room as it was August and at full capacity.The hotel was also under renovation at the time we stayed, and the reception lobby was temporarily located at a side entrance. It was small and cramped. The baggage handling staff was insufficient. We waited 30 minutes for baggage assistance upon check-out, then hauled our luggage down ourselves.The rooftop lounge is lovely, but they charged $8 for a small soda - I didn't even consider ordering a mixed drink; as I recall they were in the $15 range.The only advantage I could see to this hotel is its' fabulous location - right in the midst of several Gaudi buildings, in walking distance to everything, and in the high end shopping area, which is much quieter than the mobbed La Ramblas touristy area. We paid $269/night by booking on the hotel web site (3 nights, with the 4th one free).All in all, a disappointment because of the noise, cost of the rooftop drinks, and indifferent service.

<Author>pafcio80
<Content>Definatelly not a 5 star hotel My partner and I have returned from Barcelona two days ago where we spent 6 nights at The Majestic Hotel. When I was booking this trip, I wanted the hotel to be in a great location and at least 4-5 star. I do have to say that the location is great. It's located on a street filled with expensive stores, and lots of tapas places. You can easily walk to any major tourist attraction and if you'd like to take the metro, the stop is within a block away.After looking at the pictures of what the hotel looks like, I definitely knew that it looks luxurious. However, I was wrong. First of all, they are renovating the hotel so the photos that you see on their website of their front entrance and the lobby are not accurate. The entrance is on the side of the building and the lobby is very small. We booked a Classic Room which consisted of one room and a bathroom. The room was small with one bed that supposed to be queen size but it was full size. There were marks on the walls in some spots. The quality of the furniture was definitely not 5 star. The hotel splurged on a small flat screen tv for the room but there was no iron or an alarm clock! If we wanted to get up early we had to call the lobby every time. The bathroom was small but nice. Although within the whole time we stayed there the bulb in one of the sconces on either side of the mirror was out and they have not replaced it. Other than that, the housekeeper came every day. Cleaned the room, changed the sheets and towels.Roof deck has some great views but it's not big. It also has a pool with unheated water and it's pretty small. They serve drinks on the roof deck but the prices are outrageous. I travel a lot and never had a drink for 18 euros. Also, if you want any advice on how to get somewhere, ask the ladies at the front counter. They are the most helpful.

<Author>SupersonicFlyGirl
<Content>5 Stars?!?! You're kidding, right? I am currently staying at the Hotel Majestic. I had my business travel agent book this hotel based largely on the reviews on TripAdvisor. Upon checking in, I asked about the size of the room, as I had read some reviews complaining that some rooms were quite small. (Also, as I was checking in, I overheard 2 people trying to change rooms because they weren't happy with their first rooms). I must compliment the front desk clerk who helped me check in. She was extremely nice, but when I asked her about whether my room had a view or was a nice size, she frowned and said, that yes, indeed, I had been booked in one of the smaller rooms, but a nicer, larger room was available if I was willing to pay more. Since I have been traveling on business in Europe for more than a week and desperately needed sleep, I decided the extra charge was worth it for a better room, so I took it. While the room does have an extra sitting area, I have to say that this room is NOT of 5 star quality. There are marks on the walls, the furniture upholstery is worn, and the overall qualilty is more of a 3.5 star hotel, as far as rooms are concerned. There is also the annoying LOUD sound of water rushing through pipes on the other side of the wall of the room, approximately once an hour. The lobby area is nice, and the general location of the hotel is quite good, but as a business traveler, I really want the rooms and beds to be nice and comfortable. This marginally passes those criteria, particularly for the price for this room. Also, there is no ethernet connection so I am connected to a wireless connection that is not very reliable. Location (and some good online reviews) were the deciding factors in choosing the Majestic. However, having been here one day already, I am disappointed and wish I had gone with my first inclination to stay at the Hotel Arts. I would encourage the Hotel Majestic management to update the rooms and also encourage restaurant staff to make foreign visitors feel a bit more welcome.

<Author>MuttonHead
<Content>Nice but not spectacular Staying for 6 days. The rooms in general are typically sized for a big city, small. We upgraded when we arrived to a more expensive room because the one we were put in was among the smallest in it's range, lower floor, and smelled of smoke. I'd hate to see what the base level room looked like. Also as might be typical of Europe, although I'm not sure, there is no iron supplied in the rooms. Maybe I'm just a spoiled America. Doesn't Motel 6 have irons?Indeed the location is excellent although noisy at times. The rooms are well sound proofed but that will only go so far when it comes to a horn happy culture. It is perhaps among the best locations in Barcelona as far as access, shopping and just plain action.As for the service it was OK but not great. Turn down service seemed to have vanished after the 2nd night. Oops they must have been listening, someone just showed up while I am writing this review. Now I won't have to call for towels. Also a call for a sewing kit the other night required a second call after it the first failed. A little nerve racking when your trying to make a dinner date.The roof deck offers a great view of the city with a small pool area, well equipped fitness room, and sauna. It can get busy. Unfortunately we did not get a chance to try the restaurant but heard it is among the best in the city, and as such is difficult to get into. The included breakfast buffet is excellent.Overall it is a decent hotel but does not overachieve, I would say it is average for the price. It seems higher end hotels just keep getting more and more expensive, but the service always seems to lag if not decline. The week dollar doesn't help the perception. I'm thankful for the relatively inexpensive wine and comparable food prices because a trip to Europe these days is not for the faint of heart when it comes to affordability.

<Author>berniss
<Content>Great location...but disappointed We booked this hotel through our cruise line and felt comfortable that our 6 star cruise line would choose a very fine hotel for our stay.First the positive: the breakfast was excellent (one of the nicest we have ever had in Europe) and the location was very close to the information center, Ramblas, the tourist bus, and the Gaudi sites. Instead, it was merely a classic room (the base room) with a balcony. The room and bathroom, while tastefully done, were quite small. Other cruisers, who stayed at various four star properties in Barcelona, and visited our room, said our room was not as nice as theirs and they paid considerably less. While the room wasn't miniscule, we paid for more, according to the picture, and expected more.Additionally, there was no concierge available and when we made restaurant reservations each night with the front desk , each night the reservations were wrong. The first night, the gentleman at the desk rang the restaurant we were told no reservations were needed and to go directly to the restaurant. THere was a long line and we had to wait for 40 minutes. The next night, even though we wrote out what we needed, the time of the reservation was wrong and we found out that they made the reservation an hour earlier than we requested. There was no confirmation as we are used to in a hotel of this class.Even room service was lacking, for two days they never emptied our waste paper basket.Lastly, porterage was supposed to be included in our package, yet our porter, who was very nice, told us he was not informed of this and wanted his tip. It was very embarrassing.We have stayed at a number of four and five star hotels and were disappointed at the poor service levels and value for our money. It is certainly not what one expects of a hotel of this calibre.

<Content>Beautiful, welcoming hotel My sister and I stayed at the Hotel Majestic in Barcelona for a night this week. It was a wonderful stay. We reserved a regular room and when we went up to our room we were delighted to find that they put us in a junior suite with two balconies overlooking the Passeig de Gracia. Everything about the room was elegant and comfortable, from the sitting area to the beds to the large bathrrom with a jacuzzi tub/shower and another large shower. We came home to find a large fruit tray and a bottle of water in our room with a card welcoming us to the hotel. Our only, very slight, problem was when we decided to watch a movie in the room. There were no descriptions on the screen so we chose the only movie listed as a comedy (one we'd never heard of). It was actually a drama, somewhat of a thriller or action type movie. We mentioned that when we checked out and the man at the front desk immediately offered to take it off the bill (we declined since we had watched the movie). The people who work in the hotel were all very nice and very helpful and it's in a perfect location for seeing this beautiful city.

<Author>SuzanneGDerbyshire
<Content>Fantastic! Highly Recommended. This is a fantastic hotel, with real class and quality service.My husband and I stayed at the Majestic for three nights booking in 3rd March 2007, and from the first sight of the hotel to the last we were impressed all the way, from the look of the hotel from the outside to the well dressed doormen, amazing reception area, smart in appearance and manner are the reception staff and all very helpful and pleasant.Our room was at the front and overlooked the wonderful Passeig de Gracia, I agree with other reviews that the rooms are not large but neither are they tiny, they are very quaint but most importantly they are spotless and smart. The bed was very comfortable and it had beautiful white crisp quality bedding and there were lovely bathroom accessories which were replaced every day.We were pleasantly suprised when we were also greeted with a complimentary bottle of champagne, a lovely touch as it was my husbands birthday.We ate in the hotel on the first night in the restaurant on the ground floor, the tapas was fantastic and again the staff and service was excellent, five star plus if you ask me!We also had a drink at the bar on the roof top which does have fantastic views, and we had a drink in the bar on the ground floor listening to the wonderful tunes being played on the piano, qualtiy all around. Yes the drinks in the hotel are more than you would pay in an english bar but the views and atmosphere are well worth the price for the special occasion.I would not hesitate to recommend this to all family and friends, the hotel is immaculate, the staff are very helpful and friendly and the location is just perfect. The hotel is worth every penny, it is really worth saving up that bit extra and staying here.Thank you to all the staff at the Majestic for making our stay so special and exceeding all our expectations.

<Content>Cannot beat the location The hotel is very central. All the designer shops are within the same block- Chanel is actually built within the hotel! we opted for a superior room which was small- god knows how small the standard room was....Do not eat in the restaurant unless you have alot of money..... straters are 30-50E and mains and 50-100E's!!! there are some nice restaurants off the side strreets along the Passig De Graci. <Author>luv2travel28
<Content>Great weekend We stayed at the Majestic Hotel during a long weekend to Barcelona in July. I had read some not so good reviews on Trip Advisor but after great investigation of other hotels in the area decided that the price and location was right.The hotel is very well located right on the Passeig de Gracia. This is a large boulevard filled with designer shops and restaurants as well as Gaudi architecture and frequent stops for the tourist bus. The room was nice and the bathroom large. I had upgraded to a Superior room but like other reviewers on the site I was not sure what more I got for my money. However I liked the room and we were at the end of the hall and on a quiet street. The room had all the normal amenities that you would expect of a good hotel, toiletries, bathrobe, slippers etc. 鈥?plus a comfortable bed. The TV had a good selection of satellite channels including BBC which is unusual for European cities, we usually only get the English news channels.We did not use the gym, room service or eat at any of the restaurants but we did use the pool on the rooftop. This was a great place although a bit crowded during the late afternoon when everybody wanted to get some late sun and have a quick dip. But that was ok because I knew it would be like that and prepared myself for it. I was just pleased that it had a pool as they are hard to find in city hotels. The pool area however came into its own in the evening. After a walk along Las Ramblas (which I have to say I didn鈥檛 like 鈥?a bit too rough for me) 鈥?it was wonderful to come back to the hotel and enjoy a nice glass of wine sitting up on the rooftop overlooking the lights of the city on a beautiful summer evening. Yes it was expensive 鈥?but you get what you pay for. If I had my choice between an expensive glass of wine on the roof of the Majestic or a cheap beer on Las Ramblas, I know which I would choose.Barcelona is a great city and there is a lot to do. We took the train out to Sitges and spent the day on the beach (well a few hours 鈥?it was 40 degrees) 鈥?plus we saw all that you should see in the city by using the tourist bus which allowed us to get on and off all day. If we went back to Barcelona we would have no hesitation in staying at the Majestic again 鈥?however we never tend to return to a place twice 鈥?there are too many places in the world to see.

<Author>Nico1611
<Content>Good hotel but expensive Excellently located, just steps from it all in Barcelona, the Majestic is a true 4 star hotel. The rooms are quite functional, though standard rooms are a bit small (we had two, a standard and a nice superior). Service is overall impeccable, the fitness room on the rooftop a nice surprise, and so is the (unfortunately small) pool and the view from the roof. Breakfast is very generous, varied, and good. We didn't have a real chance to try the food at the hotel, for there is plenty of choice in Barcelona, but it seemed all right. On the down-side, this hotel is rather expensive, but the fact is accommodation is rather expensive in Barcelona, especially in the summer time... <Author>Pantani
<Content>Excellent location, good hotel Myself and a group of friends stayed for 3 nights over a weekend.All of the staff were very helpful, speaking excellent English.The location is excellent, within 150m of 2 Gaudi buildings and perhaps a mile from the Sagrada Familila, it is a very stylish part of town.The gym is more than adequate, with bikes, treadmills, stairclimbers, some free weights and a multi gym. The rooftop pool is small, more of a plunge pool than anything to swim in, but perfect to cool down in.I thought our twin room (504) was small, the beds were cosily close together !! but the room is otherwise well appointed. The walls must be thin, as I could hear the taps running in 503.The TV had Sky News, BBC 12 and ITV, plus a number of other European channels.Didn't eat in the hotel.We went to the indoor Cart racing track, it's about a Euro 25 cab ride away, I'd never done it before and thought it was great fun, if you're going, prepare to get sweaty.Clearly for any sport fans the Camp Nou is an experience not to be missed and it is easily accessible from this hotel on the Metro (which is very easy to use) or in a taxi.Taxis are cheap in Barca, but I do live in London !!!

<Author>Tagoladad
<Content>Pricey  Ok鈥ere we go鈥e left JFK airport on Thursday afternoon July 13. We had a 5:40 PM flight that arrived in Barcelona at 7:45 AM on Friday. Although JFK was a little disorganized, Delta was just great. The flight was smooth as can be. When we arrived at BCN (Barcelona airport) we waited on a very short line (maybe five minutes) to pass through customs and immigration. Our bags were waiting on the carousel and we grabbed a luggage cart (there are no sky caps at the Barcelona airport and the luggage carts are free to use, just walk to the side of the carousel and grab one) and proceeded to the taxi stand. There was a long line of taxis waiting. We knew from these boards that the fare for the cab to the Majestic Hotel should have been around 25 Euros and it was exactly that price. We arrived at the Majestic about 9:00 AM. Great Hotel. As this was our first time in Europe we had nothing to compare it to, but we have stayed in the Plaza Hotel (not so great) the Waldorf Astoria (very nice) The United Nation Plaza (very nice) in New York, The Fairmont in San Francisco (best bed we ever slept in) as well The Princess in Acapulco (beautiful grounds) so even though we鈥檝e never been to Europe we鈥檝e been to a couple of nice hotels and the Majestic was certainly nice. We had room #701, a junior suite overlooking the Passeig De Gracia, the hotel is situated between two Gaudi buildings, the Batllo and La Pedrera. The hotel is just a few blocks from the top of Las Ramblas (there are definitely hotels a lot closer to Las Ramblas) and is on both the RED and BLUE line of Bus Turistic. The staff and concierge at the hotel were excellent. Everyone speaks English, the hotel was immaculate, the staff very friendly, and the room huge. We freshened up and hit the streets. When my DW and I talked about jet lag with our friends, everyone advised us 鈥渘ot to go to sleep鈥?so we didn鈥檛. Even though we hadn鈥檛 slept the entire evening (save for a few winks on the plane) we forged ahead and went for a walk and breakfast on the Passeig De Gracia. After a nice omelet at an outdoor caf茅 we bought tickets for the Bus Turistic and made the Sagrada Familia our first stop. The church is quite impressive from the outside so we decided to go inside as well. The line in front of the bus stop was huge so my DW and I figured that we would just walk around the church, see the whole thing take a few pictures and get back on the bus. As we circled the block we found another ticket window around the corner that had absolutely no line, so we bought tickets and went inside. There is an elevator that goes to the top, but the line was very long and we didn鈥檛 want to wait. We asked if there were stairs but we were told that there weren鈥檛, so we just walked around for a little bit and left. My DW then walked through the small, limited gift shop but didn鈥檛 get anything. Across the street from the church was a great gift shop that had some really beautiful things. We went to a local supermarket in the neighborhood, walked around a little bit and then got back on the bus and made the Parc Guell our next stop. The bus stops on at the bottom of the hill several blocks from the parc. It is a long uphill climb on a very narrow street to get up to Parc Guell. It was very hot (the middle of the afternoon in the middle of July) but the views from the Parc were well worth it. The parc has a beautiful entrance (mosaic dragons and lizards line the steps) and the columns, corridors, open spaces and buildings are really incredible. The panorama overlooks all of Barcelona. Just an incredible view. There is a small snack stand with shaded umbrellas at the top where we enjoyed some ices. We then took the outside path of the parc down to the main street, which led us back down the hill to the bus stop. By now it was about 4:30 or 5:00 PM. We took the bus back to the Hotel Majestic (seeing quite a bit of the city along the way) and took a short nap and got ready for dinner at 9:00. The concierge recommended a restaurant called Botafumiero. It is a seafood restaurant that had great fish and Paella. With wine and tip, dinner for 2 was 100 Euros. Certainly not cheap, but we loved it. When we arrived at the restaurant at 9:00 PM we were one of the only diners in the restaurant. When we left at about 11:30 the place was packed. We took a cab back to the hotel to get ready for tomorrow. We woke up Saturday morning and my wife asked me to look at her watch to see what time it was. I asked her if she had changed her watch to Barcelona time. She said she had, and I said 鈥渨ell, then it鈥檚 12:15 PM. She made some comment about my age and my ability to see small numbers so I checked her cell phone and sure enough, it was 12:15. We felt great but we had slept for about 11 hours. We thought it was a small concession to the travel and the time change, went down to the internet caf茅 at the hotel (20 Euros for the duration of your stay), did our business and then I went out to get us some coffee and rolls. We are both big coffee drinkers so we didn鈥檛 mind the espresso that they serve in Spain. Got dressed and then took a cab down to the Plaza Catalunya, so that we could walk down Las Ramblas. After a few blocks of the human statues, the bird salesman and postcard kiosks, we took a left hand turn and entered the Barri Gotic (the Gothic Quarter). We found ourselves in front of a beautiful church and sat down at a caf茅 (Estruch) for pizza and salad. The plaza was a beautiful place to have lunch and watch the action. After lunch we began our search for the Picasso Museum. We only had the map from the Bus turistic (and because the museum is not one of their stops, it鈥檚 not on the map) so we really weren鈥檛 sure where it was. We saw some signs pointing in the general direction of the museum and we gladly followed. The time that we spent lost (there is no other word for it. We didn鈥檛 know where we were or where we were going) in the Barri Gotic was magical. We loved it. We found wine shops (you can bring wine on the ship, but I鈥檒l talk about that later), alleyways, incredible architecture, friendly people and eventually the Picasso Museum. The line was about 25 minutes and the entrance fee about 8 or 10 Euros. My wife loved the museum and all of Picasso鈥檚 works. I鈥檓 not as sophisticated as she is, so she tolerated my opinions for the 45 minutes we toured the museum. After we left we walked toward Port Vell. It was a pretty good walk to the port, but we were there to see Barcelona so we didn鈥檛 mind. The port is fantastic. I鈥檓 not sure which part was old and which parts were built for the 1992 Olympics, but the cool breeze, open space and views of the Marina were beautiful. We walked all the way down (and it was a pretty long walk) to the bus stop for the Bus Turistic. By now it was 8:00 PM (although it seemed like the middle of the day) so we took the bus back to the Batllo (the stop closest to our hotel) and got ready for dinner. We wanted to visit an acquaintance in Barcelona so we asked the concierge to change our dinner reservation at Aqua to 10:30 PM. By the time we finished our visit and got down to Agua (a great restaurant on the beach) it was after 11:00 PM. The hostess wasn鈥檛 too happy that we were so late for our reservation so she made us wait till 11:30 for our table. We sat at the table closest to the Mediterranean and settled in. By the time our food came it was midnight and the restaurant was still packed. I guess it鈥檚 true鈥hey have dinner at midnight in Barcelona. Food was very good (service just OK). Wife had fish, I had chicken. With wine and tip, about 65 Euros. Grabbed a cab back to the hotel about 1:30 AM to get ready to board the Jewel in the morning. I guess that since we were doing a pre-cruise, we should have packed our luggage with that in mind. I would definitely recommend packing a bag for your pre-cruise and then packing bags for your cruise. We spent a lot of time on Sunday morning having to repack all of our luggage. On Sunday morning, again, I went down to the Fresh and Ready (that was the name) to get coffee and croissants. After breakfast and packing we left our bags with the hotel to do a little last minute sightseeing. We stopped in the Casa Batllo (a famous Gaudi building on the Passeig De Gracia) for only a moment. From the brief glimpse we had it was great. We bought a few souvenirs, took a stroll around the neighborhood (everything was closed on Sunday morning. The streets were deserted) and then went back to the hotelWe didn't eat at the hotel nor did we order room service. The staff was incredible. Very friendly. Very Helpful. Always interested. Never seemed like they were too good to help us. Rooftop pool area is really cool. Great views of the city. Nice gym. The Hotel was immaculate. Bed was tremendous. There is a 3 for 2 night special so make sure you take advantage of it. Three nights at the hotel were 800 Euros. Location was incredible. Nicest section of city.For any questions email me at Tagoladad@aol.com and put BARCELONA QUESTION in the subject line

<Author>BonnieGo
<Content>Loved the Majestic! We are a family of 3 who stayed in a suite at the Majestic 3 nights precruise. The suite was huge! It was like staying in your own apartment. The suite was very nicely decorated with one bedroom with a comfortable king bed, balcony, and plasma tv, livingroom with plasma tv, 2 bathrooms, small oval office with desk and comfortable chairs surrounded with sliding windows that looked out over Passeig de Gracia. There was a large entranceway with lots of closet space. There were double doors to block out noise. My son slept in a roll away bed that wasn't too comfortable. One suggestion that I would like to make is that this room should have a convertable couch which turns into a bed. If it had this kind of couch then this suite would sleep 5 which is hard to find in Barcelona.The staff were wonderful. We had lost luggage and at my request they frequently called the airlines to check on the status. They reassured me and delivered my luggage promptly when it arrived the next morning. We opted not to do the breakfast plan because it was too expensive. There was a wonderful cafe across the street where they had great pastries, coffee, and fresh squeezed orange juice. The rooftop area was beautiful with a great view, but the drinks were very expensive. A soda cost $9 euros. Great location near hop on/hop off bus, and many restaurants. From reading other reviews I think that if you stay in a jr suite or suite then the Majestic is a positive experience, a standard or deluxe room is less satisifying. I didn't see a deluxe or standard room so can't comment on them. Would stay here again if they keep the stay 3 pay for 2 nights special.

<Author>durhamsue
<Content>peaceful elegance We stayed at the Majestic for 3nights july 2006, we had been fortunate to book through an easyhotels special offer and received a comfortable discount which included breakfast. We certainly recommend breakfast plenty of choice and all very fresh. After reading various reports on tripadvisor we arrived open minded. The entrance and main rooms and staff of the hotel are 5 star but the bedrooms are more 4 star. As it was a very hot week, we were pleased to be at the back of the hotel (no view but very quiet) in an air-conditioned room which had large very comfortable bed and small seating area, flat screen tv with full uk channels. Decor of the room could have been more opulent but was fine for the price we paid, more crown plaza than intercontinental! However, the staff were very courteous and helpful. The view from the rooftop terrace at night is fantastic, because the drink prices include small pre-dinner snacks they are pricy however we paid the same for a beer (9euro) on the Ramblas, no comparison, the wine and cocktail prices might be a little steep for some pockets.e.g. (20 euro) The hotel is next to a metro and many of the cultural attractions. We would recommend the official barcelona bus 18 euro for 1 day 22euro for 2 days, fantastic value as we went from each attraction, waiting no more than 2 mins for next bus, being able to see sights of Barcelona as we travelled. Taxi from airport was 25euro but after meeting friends we returned from place catalunya (5 mins from hotel) on airport bus (regular) 2.75 euro. driver was not as scary! We stay in many city hotels and would certainly return to the Majestic.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Best Hotel in the world....... I have had the pleasure of staying at the Majestic Hotel in Barcelona twice now. In terms of sheer quality, comfort and customer service you will be hard pressed to find many hotels that can match it. The location is excellent for a nice stroll into the town centre and is also near to the metro. Rooms are absolutely spotlessly clean with effective air conditioning and blackout curtains. The breakfast buffet is simply vast and totally delicious. They will also look after your bags after you check out until you are ready to head off to the airport which is a very useful service. The roof terrace has spectacular 360 degree views of Barcelona, with a bar and small pool. I had my wedding ceremony on this roof terrace in June 2006 which the Majestic helped to organise along with a superb cocktail reception. If you want to stay in style and luxury then the Majestic is well worth splashing out on. All staff are very friendly, helpful and polite and there is a really nice cool and calm atmosphere about the place. In my opinion it is the best hotel in the world!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel, unfortunate city Stayed in mini suite... worth extra expense, judging from poor experience of those in classic rooms. Our room(s) were cleaned well, somewhat spacious, furnished acceptably. The King bed was two sep beds cobbled together and one could tell that, but it was ok... perhaps too hard for our taste. We found staff to be very helpful and upbeat. They really were a major plus of our stay at Hotel. The bar and food service were acceptable and accomodating. Food prep was quite good if not the best. We were not disappointed with our stay, and might well use Hotel again, because of its location and its staff. In no less than a mini suite however. We found the city of Barcelona to smell (sewerage) almost every other block. The city is not a clean city. It has a kind of dog eared quality to it that must have shined brightly at one point but is definitely over the hill now. Whole city needs housekeeping. Ramblas et al is ok, but same commercial greenway situation is found in a number of cities. Streets, walks chronically crowded. Signage is desparately unhelpful and I can't think of any attraction that does not have a superior conterpart in other cities and locations (beach, mouuntain park, cathedrals, winding old town alleyways, as charming as can be, full of folks wishing to sell you something). We caught some ladies in process of lifting our wallets in street. But this can happen anywhere. Nice town, but not unique. The grubbiness of the city overwhelms what ever charm it maintains (and there really is some). This city has amazingly good PR. But we cannot recommend it. Won't be back.Wish the Majestic existed in different city.

<Author>Shant
<Content>Majestic Arrogance I travel to Barcelona very regularly, and I chose to stay at the Majestic recently, only down to its location and promised services...... and also a curiosity from having passed the hotel on several occasions. I would say that the hotel is very average in every way. It is an old hotel, hence you cannot expect huge functional rooms. Their website tells you classic rooms are 20 sq metres...they do not hide the fact that their classic rooms are tiny, however, images on their website are not representative of the actual rooms, for instance, the bathroom in the image under classic room is not the bathroom you will receive; the bathroom will actually be very small and will require the agility of a gymnast to navigate. When I brought this up, the point was ignored. Wireless internet was also advertised.....could I get reception? Only by holding my laptop in the air at a strange angle, in a strange position!For a 5 star hotel, the bar is reasonably priced. The food may perhaps be decent....they will tell you that Drolma has a Michelin star, however, when hot food is served very cold after a very long wait, it is difficult to ascertain quality (and no apologies made either).5 star? Well, yes and no. In Spain, stars are awarded convincingly on facilities, not quality. I have not often experienced such average 5 star facilities with tacky unimaginative decor, but they do what they do and they do it well enough to run a 鈥榮uccessful鈥?hotel.Having had a look at the better rooms, I would suggest only staying here if you were prepared to pay the extra for an upgraded room. I would suggest staying elsewhere rather than a classic room unless you are supremely interested in location and you are not bothered by impolite staff and ineffective service, though the classic rooms are very cheap, so this may sway you. If you want good service and a good all round experience, stay elsewhere.I would perhaps make some suggestions to the hotel, however, I have read some of the responses made to other reviewers on this website, and I find these to be rude, unhelpful and argumentative.... similar to the attitude when face to face with the front desk staff. I would rather just move on to a different hotel than waste any more time with this hotel. Barcelona is a lovely, bustling city, so the Majestic will not really have a problem filling beds, however, some time in the future, they may need to rethink things.

We were treated like royalty from the staff of the hotel. For example, they helped us book a great Flamenco show and got us front row seats. The rooms were beautifully appointed and so comfortable. There is a fabulous bed with a duvet and feather pillows and black out drapes that really worked to darken the room. Even our location on the street was dead quiet thanks to double paned windows. The hotel is in a great location, in the more upscale part of downtown but within easy walking distance of everything. The tourist bus stop was a block up the street and was the crossing of the two main lines. If they are running a 3 for 2 nights special like we got, you can enjoy a real five star hotel for a great price.

<Author>jennifer91001
<Content>Beautiful Hotel, Great Location, and Hard beds We just returned from a one week stay at the Majestic in Barcelona. I stayed here about 4 years ago and decided to stay again based on the hotels old world charm and it's location. We booked through the hotels web-site and paid 205Euro+7%VAT per night breakfast included along with a one day pass on the Barcelona touristic(hop-on, hop-off)bus. The hotel was still as beautiful as I remembered and the location is wonderful. We enjoyed the daily breakfast and also the little old man that plays the piano nightly in the bar. One thing that I didn't recall on my last visit was the rock hard beds. Not only me but the other 4 people that I traveled with all complained that the beds were hard. We all slept in rooms with twin beds so we can't comment on the larger beds but we all think that the management of the Majestic should spend a night sleeping or should I say trying to sleep on one of these beds. Even though the beds leave much to be desired and the desk staff fail to say hello when you happen to catch their eye, I still love this hotel-hard beds and all. Please make sure to visit the cafe located to the left of the hotel 5-10 feet past the cross walk. We enjoyed spanish hot chocolate rich and thick. And, you must stop for Gellato at one of the many places you'll see as you walk the streets of Barcelona. We ate at Citrus restaurant located near the hotel but wouldn't recommend it as the food was expensive, the portions were small and they gave us the wrong check and it took them over 30 minutes to find someone who undestood the problem. You might want to consider taking the airport bus to the city as it's very affordable and convient. We walked right outside the airport terminal and took the bus from the airport(3.60 Euro)to Placa de Cataluna and walked straight up the street to the hotel. On our way back to the airport we caught the airport bus at the stop near Burberry's which was a shorter walk from the hotel(you'll see the airport bus logo on the bus shelter). NOTE: The bus only stops at this stop when going to the airport.
