<Author>Zuerich
<Content>avoid "classic" rooms We left that property with very mixed emotions. The reason for booking it was the exceptional location: close to everything within walking distance there is no better choice under that point of view. But apart from that I think that there is no reason to stay there. My wife arrived a day before me, being a young, single travelling women. Was it a coincidence that she was given the room next to the elevator, courtyard facing with a very strange, convoluted layout with a small window in the corner between the bathroom and the wall, so it was like a room without a window? Of course somebody has to take the bad rooms, but why allocate it to somebody who has booked for 5 days and not to somebody who just spends there one night? So we were given another room. As we opened the door, a wave of very bad, acidic smell came out. We called the front desk and the person who came round wrinkled his nose and admitted, that there was a terrible smell, assuming that it was the new carpet of the remodelled room. Well, if their new carpets smell like this, I dont want to know about the old ones 鈥?br/>Room number three, not expecting much anymore, was very small too. Between the bed and the bathroom there was the desk with a minibar, a small table with two chairs and the closet with a rack for a small suitcase. Furnished like this, there was no space for putting a regular suitcase on the floor leaving space for walking around it so that we either had to close it and put it uprigth or climb over it when we wanted to go to the bathroom. Truly exciting when you have to get up at night. Now we definitiely were ready for a drink. But the minibar/refrigerator was not working. As we do not like warm drinks we called for ice cubes (no ice-machines in the corridor) and maintenance. The electrician arrived before the waiter and fixed it. Than the ice-bucket came and we were informed, that we had to pay 5 Euros for it. For a bucket we needed, because the fridge was broken and the drinks were too warm? In a 5 star property? Come on, that鈥檚 realy bad style and cheesy. Beeing very small, the air in the room was sticky. Usually we like to leave the windows open. But in this case we preferred not to, because the fire stairs were crossing the window. So we switched on the A/C. There was air coming out of the outlet but it was warm. We put the thermostat to the minimum, but still only warm air. We asked several times for reparation at the front desk, but nothing happened. Why not offer to have another room with a working A/C? The best thing about the room was the housekeeping. Very efficient and immaculatly clean all the time. The toilet was tucked between the washbasin and the wall so that one had to squeeze himself diagonally on it. The lobby, bar and restaurant were very stylish and arranged tastefully. The breakfast room is located in the basement (no windows). The food-quality was very good and the service very efficient. On our visits the breakfast room was crowded and the acoustics were quiet bad so that the overall experience was not very pleasant. The female front-desk staff were very nice and helpful, whereas male stuff were rather presumptuos. Example? We were asking for directions one morning, when suddenly the employee turned away from us starting a conversation with somebody more interesting than us. Probably the stay would have been better, if we had booked a de luxe room (130 Euros more per night). But how could we know before? When booking in a 5-Star property one can expect a certain size and standard even in the least expensive room. But the 鈥瀋lassic鈥?rooms in my opinion are definitely substandard in terms of size, layout and location. Of course in the hotels website it鈥檚 noticed that they are only 鈥瀉pproximately 20 square meters鈥?(they should add, that they are dark and the samll window only gives a view in a grim courtyard) what would be barely acceptable if of regluar shape. But in such a tubular or strange layout, it's much worse and clearly not acceptable. In my opinion, the very narrow rooms I have seen, should only be furnished with a small bed and sold as single rooms only, as for two persons they defintively are unreasonable in a 5-Star property. Next time in Barcelona we will go somewhere else.

<Author>toptourist
<Content>Not as 'majestic' as it looks! Have just returned from 3 nights at the Majestic in Barcelona. We had booked 3 nights for the price of 2 with Last Minute, but most people on this site seem to have got a much better deal!! On arrival, it had the feel of a five star place - lovely lobby, stunning flower arrangments and a guy to greet us and carry our cases in. These impressions were, in my opinion, about all that was 5 star about the place. We were not lucky enough to be offered an upgrade to a junior suite, even though I explained that the trip was for my husband's 50th - which it was, - consequently we had quite a small room! (I have stayed in larger rooms in a Premier Lodge in England, and that's saying something!)The bathroom required the skills of an expert contortionist when getting in and out of the bath - you literally had to climb over the toilet. You also needed elasticated arms to check the temperature of the water in the bath and shower, as the glass shower door is immoveable - because there is simply nowhere to move it to. It was a real squash. We also had to shift a table and two armchairs whenever we wanted to open the wardrobe! Not my idea of 5 star!. Having said all of this, the room was clean, nicely decorated and regularly serviced. The other thing that I found tricky was the traffic noise, but I suppose you should expect this in a big city. We were on the 8th floor (room 822, if you wish to avoid it!!!) and could still hear the roar of the traffic. (because I spend a lot of time in hotels when I work, I had earplugs, and even these din't block the noise out entirely.) We could also hear the conversations of the people in room 821 - word for word, actually, and I wouldn't have said that they were particularly raucous. You could even hear them tapping their tooth brushes against the basin - and we are not serial evesdroppers, you just couldn't miss it.I thought the location of the hotel was good - very near a metro station and plenty of buses and cabs nearby. We didn't take breakfast in the hotel, preferring a cafe down the road, with all the local people. I liked the piano bar in the hotel, but as others have said, it was dear. A beer and a glass of cava came to 15 euros. However, I enjoyed the atmosphere in there and the piano guy was great. We ate in the hotel restaurant one night. This was a slightly surreal experience, as it was just us and one other couple, but the service was friendly, the wine and food were excellent, and we didn't have far to go after the meal was over! Other places that we ate (which we had chosen from The Rough Guide to Barcelona) were El Glop, which was excllent, El Muscletaria (fantastic place selling just - you guessed it - mussels - and also clams), and a fabulous, fabulous restaurant called 'anima', in which I had one of the best meals that I have ever had in my life. All three restaurants were well worth seeking out, and were packed full of locals, so obviously not just for tourists! I really, really enjoyed Barcelona, especially Parc Guell, the Gaudi House near to the Majestic Hotel, the Miro Fundacion and La Seu, with the views from the rooftop and the geese in the peaceful courtyard.I would like to return to the city. In truth I do not think I would stay at the Majestic again, as on this occasion I did not think we got what we paid for, and that would be my main gripe. Maybe I wasn't canny enough when I booked! I would prefer to find a cheaper hotel that was a bit more honest about what it offered and was better value for money.  
<Date>Feb 13, 2006

<Author>Harpesharp
<Content>Excellent for shopping We stayed at Hotel Majestic for 3 nights from 19th Jan 2006. We booked a junior suite for 385 Euros per night directly with hotel using the 3 nights for price of 2 nights offer. Managed to get Breakfast thrown aswell which is not cheap.The hotel is excellently position on one of the upmarket streets of Barcelona called Passeig de Gracia. This is prime shopping belt and the flagship Zara store did very well after my wife had been sales shopping there. Also close to a Gaudi building which you can view inside and not far from Metro if you don't want to walk too far. Taxi's are not too expensive either. Top of Ramblas are is a 10 minutes walk.The hotel was nice, but not as opulent as that of the one in Rome that we stayed at. The Drolma restaurant was excellent but very expensive and only recommend if it is a special occasion. We also went to other excellent restaurants like the Fernandez (5 minutes from hotel), Barcelonetta (in marina area), and Tapas Tapas.We were well looked after and had good advice from Guest Relations. The room was spacious and had good views of the main road (make sure you ask for a room with this view). Air conditioning was not great more of a heater and did not pump out cold air. Bring a travel iron as they don't have them, they did kindly supply a steam iron - but this kept tripping the electricity supply! Bathroom great for this room type, great shower and also an additional bath with hydrojets to relax after much walking. Worth it if for a special occasion, beware the temptation of too much shopping, lucky we had a spare suitcase.

<Author>snoopy82
<Content>Fantastic location! The majestic was excellently located for a weekend of exploring barcelona. Some of Gaudi's most infamous buildings are within view of the hotel itself. The rooftop pool area offers amazing views, especially of the sagrada cathedral, and a prime sunbathing spot for those afternoon siestas. The pool is a little small but this was not a problem as there are a million things, other than swimming to fill your time with whilst in barcelona. The service was exceptional, the staff helpful and accomadating at all requests. We had a superior room which was modern, comfortable and stylish, although not on a par in terms of luxury with some other 5 star rooms we have encountered. The bar and restaurants are very expensive but easily avoidable as there are a wealth of alternatives in the surrounding area. We would definitely reccomend this hotel to anyone wanting a 5 star city break in barcelona.

<Author>pj270744
<Content>High prices at the Majestic. We were recommended to the Majestic Hotel by a Barcelona native but found our stay was affected by the very high prices both for food and for the bar. We suspect, that as the hotel is used by the business crowd, the two restaurants and bar are geared towards people on expense accounts. The price for the buffet breakfast is a very high 20+ euros and the prices for the Drolma restaurant are as much as 40+ euroes for a main course. The bar prices were also very high and a small bottle of diet coke was 6 euros. Having said that the room was very comfortable and very quiet. The staff were friendly and helpful. My wife and I found that the best option was to simply walk a few yards to one of several cafes where we could get breakfast and that we ate dinner either at one of several good restaurants in the area or took the metro down the the port area. Sumsum, opposite the hotel is recommended.

<Author>GoodGuyBob
<Content>Great location, beware lower floors Stunning exterior. Room decor was very nice. Mini bar refrigerator came in very handy. An annoyance: the bathtub/shower has a partial wall (covers about the first third), so when you shower, water can spray all over the bathroom floor (why not install a shower curtain instead?). Rooftop pool is small, but the fact that there even IS a pool is greatly appreciated. Another annoyance was that we had no view. We were in room 338 (4th floor to Americans) our window faced another building (like maybe 10 feet away). So we really couldn't even see the sky. I'd suggest that you ask for something on the 5th floor or higher, or better still, ask about a room in the front of the building.Regarding the surroundings, Passeig de Gracia has many high end clothing stores in the vicinity. About 2 blocks north is Gaudi's La Pedrera an absolute MUST do -- it's amazing (allow at least an hour). A block south is a smaller Gaudi building (but I didn't visit it). A subway station is 3 blocks north (the Diagonal station). Note about the subway, some of the subway lines have levers on the sliding doors. If you see a lever, you will have to turn it for the door to open (either boarding the subway, or exiting it). Dining out a couple blocks south is Tapa Tapa which we didn't care for. A trick they use is to provide you with bread topped with tomato sauce. This is NOT free. They also gave us a bowl of olives which we sent back. But we thought the bread was included and was not.Next to Tapa Tapa is Citrus, which is upstairs. Here the bread actually IS included, and we had a very good meal.Across the street is Tenorio, which has a delicious goat cheese salad (a must get). But Tenorio hit us with TWO extras that we had to pay for...again the bread topped with tomato (you'd think we'd learn!) and a cheese plate (which was delicious). However, these two items probably added 10 Euros to our total bill.Also just south of the hotel are several inexpensive places for a quick bite, such as McDonald's, Fresh  Ready, and another place across the street.Oh, and for a large selection of yummy Italian gelato, visit Arlequin gelateria which is right across from Gaudi's Sagrada Familia another MUST DO (and do go up the elevator for stunning views as well).Oh and one more must do, visit Placa Espana for the fountain show after dark on weekends. I think this may have been the inspiration for the Fountains of Bellagio in Las Vegas. They have a fountain show correographed to colored lights and music -- it's wonderful.Oh, one more lesson learned. The taxi from the airport to Hotel Majestic is roughly 20 to 23 Euros and is metered. We took a cruise, and after the cruise took a taxi to the airport. The distance to the airport is the same, but the taxis turned off their meters and charged us a whopping 35 Euros to take us to the airport -- almost double of what it would have been if it was a metered ride (AND he was bold enough to ask for a tip!). If your cruise ship offers transportation, you may save money going that route. Otherwise, you are totally at the mercy of the taxis at the port -- you have no other choice, so they can charge whatever they feel like.None-the-less, Barcelona is a clean and wonderous city -- I could live there! Enjoy!  
<Date>Sep 15, 2005

We actually upgraded our room from a classic before travelling as a result of reviews on this site - thanks for the tip - it was worth it. Tried Drolmar - the Michelin starred restaurant on the last night - great one off experience - incredible service, great food but rediculous price in view of the great food nearby. The only disappointing thing about this hotel was the presence of plastic flowers and plants - in the main foyer, beside the lift, in the room - surely a 5 star hotel in a Barcelona could stretch to real flower arrangements in public areas and they'd be better to dump the plastic plants in the rooms - ours was put out of sight for the duration of our stay. The pool is small but had a lively crowd hanging out on Sunday evening and the gym was well equipped. All in all - 5 star except for the flowers.

<Content>Fabulous Hotel Just returned from 4 nights in The Majestic. I must say I was extremely impressed with the hotel and it's service. The pool on the roof is small, but is just really used to cool off when you've been lying on one of the lougers enjoying the stunning view. The location is ideal.... 10 minutes walk from La Rambla (although personally I didn't like it) and the main square. The tourist buses pass the hotel.We didn't eat in the hotel (it IS quite expensive for food and drink... but hey, it's 5 star) but there are loads of excellent Tapas Bars and restaurants nearby. There's a great restaurant just acrooss the street and right a little called Costa Galicia... excellent, and another to the opposite and to the left calle Tenorio...also excellent.A couple of reviewers have also mentioned the staff being unfriendly. We never passed a member of staff from check-in staff to cleaners without them saying hello and smiling (and we WERE asked if we had a nice stay as we checked out.So, it's quite expensive, but we'd do it again... becouse we're worth it!

<Author>drdkc
<Content>Great location, full service hotel Stayed at the Majestic for 4 days, in the beginning of August. The hotel has a great location, right on the Passeo de Gracia. Very central to La Ramblas,the Bari Gothic, (old city) and whatever bus or metro you might need. There was always a taxi available as well. The hotel has a rooftop plunge pool and some deck lounges although they were usually taken. There was massage available, although we didn't use the service. The hotel has a business center, and for 15 euros for your stay, you have unlimited use of the internet. We chose to use the internet cafe around the corner for 1.50 euro an hour. A better deal for us. Our room was a small room facing the side street so there a balcony and light. Some noise from the street at night, but not enough to keep us awake. There was more noise from the occasional boiserous group exiting the elevator that was right across from our room. The bathroom was fine, a bit small but with a bidet, bathtub and shower. The robe was a bit worn, and for a 5 star hotel, they really should replace them. It was really out of place for a hotel with Armani in the lobby. All in all, the rate was reasonable, it was stay three nites, get the fourth one free, and the rate was $229 euros. The buffet at the hotel was 20 euros pp. so we were happy to go outside to one of the wonderful cafes for a great breakfast for half the price. I would definitely recommend the Majestic for the location, and the service if you like a big hotel. We tend to prefer boutique style hotels that have a more personal feel, but we really did like the location.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location and above average hotel in Barcelona We stayed at the Hotel Majestic for ten days in July and were very pleased with the location as it is central to most of the shopping, cultural centres, art galleries, museums and restaurants. It is only a short walk to the metro which makes most attractions accessible in no time at all.We had booked a deluxe room and on our arrival the people manning the reception desk were most helpful and courteous. Our room was spacious, well-appointed, and quiet. The bathroom and the dressing area are bright and modern with a powerful shower. It has a large balcony which we hardly used as we were out most of the time. The TV is fairly standard and a port is available for connecting a laptop to the internet at high speed. We were provided with a cable to hook to our laptop and paid only 15 euros for the whole duration of our stay. With the heat in Barcelona at this time of the year in the high 30, we were very pleased to have a very efficient air-conditioning system.However, conveniences that are standard in most hotels - in-room coffee maker, cups, sugar, spoons and coffee - are not provided. Nor is an ironing board and iron provided, perhaps not to undermine the system in place, as the charges for having your clothes pressed are extravagant, especially for same day service. We actually checked to find out why this room service is not provided and we were told for security reasons. We asked what was meant by it but we could not get a plausible answer.We had problems with the TV and the broadband service but one call and maintenance was there to fix them immediately. Our general impression of the hotel was one of indifference; rarely were we greeted with a hello or a smile or any interest shown in whether our stay was agreeable or not. At check out, we paid the bills and still no one asked whether our stay was a pleasant one and whether we had enjoyed Barcelona. We paid and we left...With the right room, one can have a very pleasant stay at this hotel as its location is really wonderful but it has a lot of work to do in terms of personal relations. If it manages to improve its PR and succeeds in making its guests welcome, we would rate it as an excellent hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Warning - don't book a classic room! We booked a 4 night stay at the Majestic based on the excellent reviews received on Tripadvisor. Having re read the reviews - everybody that raved about the rooms appeared to have booked a junior suite (or certainly NOT a classic room!). We booked a classic room and having looked on the hotel website it looked great.On arriving that the hotel (on the plus side - the location was great) the receptionist, on seeing that we had booked a classic room, immediately suggested that we upgrade to a bigger and lighter room for a mere extra 60 euros per night. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beware the Majestic! Preview your room if you must stay! Ok, so after reading all the glowing reviews on TripAdvisor, my wife and I booked into this hotel. I am sorry to say we were deeply disappointed. Room 822.I write this, so as to give other potential clients of the hotel fair warning.Firstly the Good:Location is fantastic, on the Passeig de Gracia an easy walk to the Rambla and a block from the Metro station. The reception and entrance is grand; flowers, marble, efficient staffThe porter service, very sharp and friendly.The Bad:I think this may all have been the unfortunate (intentional or not) allocation of a terrible room. - The room was tiny, even by European standards (We have traveled a lot). The small table and chair infringed on the cupboard, so if one wanted to access the cupboard, you had to move the furniture.- The bathroom was even smaller, my wife and I could not be in this room together. The toilet is right next to the bath/shower, so getting out the shower was a challenge, and some dexterity was required to stand in the available space. Also mildew abounded in the shower- The bed creaked and squeaked. This was partially corrected by housekeeping.- Our room on the 8th floor was underneath the top floor restaurant, so every night at midnight the sound of dragging furniture woke us up. Calling the reception to complain got a quizzical response and the promise to send someone up to investigate 鈥?I never received a response to this.- The air-conditioning system is archaic. Every time the thermostat kicked in, the air turned on loudly, and when cool, turned off, loudly again, keeping up awake.- Upon checkout, they were very efficient at billing us, but not once were we asked about our stay. I did complete a survey, and wonder if anyone will see this?So in general, it was a disaster. This is certainly NOT a 5 star hotel. The glossy exterior belies what is inside. At 225 Euros per night, it is certainly not cheap either and I am sure better value can be found elsewhere. Suggestion: If you insist on staying, view your room beforehand!!

<Author>borntotravel068
<Content>Great hotel, fantastic location We have just returned from Barcelona staying 3 nights at the Majestic .. What a fabulous hotel! Before going to Barcelona I was unsure as to whether or not I should have booked The Arts, I'm so glad I didn't. The location of the Majestic is perfect, within walking distance to all the major tourist attractions. If we had stayed at The Arts we would have needed to spend a lot more on transport just to get around Barcelona as it really is out of the way. Everyone at the hotel is friendly and the service is great. The room was adequate - we had booked a superior and I'm not quite sure what we got for the extra we paid - but as we were out all day sightseeing and only came back to change or to sleep it didn't matter. Having the outdoor rooftop pool was also a great advantage after a day walking round Barcelona! My only criticism was that breakfast seemed expensive, but again that didn't matter as we walked to a nearby pavement cafe to have breakfast there and watch the world go by. All in all, a fabulous hotel with what I would have thought to be the best location in Barcelona!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Both stately and up-to-date A friend and I recently stayed at The Majestic, which is located in the stunning EIXAMPLE section of Barcelona. We loved the location because we were within walking distance of many places we wanted to vist. Just up the street was Gaudi's La Pedrera (Casa Mila) and in the other direction Placa de Catalunya, the Gothic quarter with the magnificent Cathedral and Palau de la Musica. We had wonderful stores and small restaurants and tapas bars in all directions.We stayed in a junior suite, which was extremely comfortable. The seating area had plush chairs and a sofa, which enabled us to relax after sightseeing. Although we were on the second floor overlooking the Passeig de Gracia, the room was quiet. From our windows we could look across the street at some of the area's beautiful Modernista buildings.The breakfast buffet in a window-less but comfortable lower level was sumptous and got us started for the day. There were such typical Spanish dishes as Serrano ham and tortillas (made with potatoes). There were many kinds of pastries. I even had a fried egg because of the gorgeous organge yolks. Then I added a small baked potato half (topped with olive oil), something I have never had for breakfast.Once we stopped in the lobby lounge for coffee and another time for a light supper. We didn't get to try the expensive and very elegant restaurant Drolma. Access to a computer in the business center really worked for me. For Euros 15, I could use the internet as much as I wanted during my stay. It was great not looking at the clock when sending e-mails.The 24-hour rooms service certainly responded for us at 4:30am when I called for coffee and tea before our early morning departure. Another time when I needed a doctor, the front desk had an English-speaking doctor at my door within 20 minutes.This is a fine hotel with rates that are fair.

<Author>TxTxAustin
<Content>Great Experience for a family of 4! We booked 2 nights at the Majestic at the end of our Mediterranean cruise. We stayed in 1 junior suite and 1 regular connecting room with our 2 children. There is more than ample space in these rooms! The junior suite had a huge shower, with great water pressure. We were on the 6th floor, facing the main street, and the noise never bothered us (and I'm a light sleeper). Although expensive, room service was fabulous. We booked a package which included tourist bus tickets and breakfast each morning. The breakfast was WONDERFUL !!! There is plenty of selection for everyone, and the juice, coffee and pastries were amazing. The location is great; surrounded by high-end stores and easy walking distance to many activities. We caught the tourist bus only once, but it is nearby and easy to use. An aside: our children weren't fond of the food selections in Barcelona, so it was a big plus that the Majestic had some great offerings! If you're traveling with kids, you might want to ask where to get pizza. Even the pasta was a bit strong for them...made with anchovies. We found the Majestic to be a very nice, clean hotel with super staff.

<Author>mustardmindy
<Content>Fantastic Hotel! My husband and I stayed at the Majestic for May 23 - 27th. We booked a Jr. Suite through Expedia (based largely on the reviews on this website) and the room was wonderful, on the 5th floor facing the Gran Via (main street). It was on the southeastern side of the building (room 504?) and had two sets of double doors with 2 beautiful small wrought iron balconies overlooking the street. The room and bathroom were spacious and there were double doors that could be closed between the bedroom and sofa area. Everyone who worked at the hotel spoke very good english and the roof top pool and view couldn't be beat - great partial view of Sagrada Familia. The fitness room was very nice - treadmills with t.v.s on them with CNN. Our friends were staying in the Claris (1 block away) and even though they had the nicest room there, it was dark and smaller and the rooftop did not have near as nice a view (although their restaurant on top had great - but pricey - food) Room service was always pleasant - they sent someone to fix our t.v. at 1am! And the location could not have been beaten. Overall a great experience. As an aside, after the first 2 days there was banging in the room above us. We complained and the manager moved us to another Jr. Suite, this time on the 6th floor - room 611. The balconies were not as nice but the room was the same. Right after we moved, there was banging from the other side of the building. We called the manager back and he put us in a large suite which was VERY nice. The room was near the southeastern corner facing the main street, room 602 I think. So if you experience problems, ask for an upgrade and they might give it to you! Or book the main suite - well worth it!!!

<Content>Loved the Majestic We spent March 10-13 at the Majestic. Booked on the hotels web site and found some good prices. We were planning a romantic weekend so went for the Jr suite. My husband and I thought this hotel was just great. The room was large and nicely decorated. Bathroom was great. Bottle of Cava on ice waiting for our arrival. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>First class service, beautiful views, perfect holiday As a seasoned traveler, I am often critical of hotels - whilst trying not to be. 5 years in Dubai (where 7 star service and hotels are the norm) and the luxury of experiencing some true hotel stars (Soneva Fushi, Madives; Lanesborough  Mandarin Oriental Park Lane) means that I'm probably too critical. I was surprised then to love the Majestic - for service it is up there with the world's best. Arriving (and leaving the hotel) the friendliness of reception and porterage was impeccable - nothing was too much trouble from looking after luggage well beyong check out, to welcoming us with a warmth that will stay with us a long time (we had advised of our anniversary on booking). We stayed in Room 321 (I think) with a beautiful balcony overlooking the Passage de Gracias. Room service was very fast (Club Sandwich wonderful, though vegetable soup needed more flavour). Breakfast was not perfect for Brits (but for most Europeans our desire for toast and English sausages is probably incomprehensible (have suggested Twynings English Breakfast Tea too to management). In the end we opted for the continental breakfast which had the most gorgeous cakes we experienced in Barcelona - one with creme de Catalan. This was our first trip to Barcelona and we opted for the Majestic pack including tourist bus ticket (cannot recommend this highly enough). On arrival at the hotel we were greeted with a beautiful book on the Passsage de Gracia as a present and a lovely bottle of Vintage Cava. The message said simly welcome home. The room may not have been the prettiest or most luxurious we have stayed in, there may not have been in-room tea and coffee facilities, but the service, attention to detail, view and wonderful staff made these insignificant. Oh and it has the best location of any hotel in Barcelona, no question. For a perfect visit to Barcelona - and to find a home away from home, we recommend the Majestic highly

<Author>onthetrail
<Content>Good location, not really deluxe 5* though Just got back from 3 days in Barcelona, staying at the Majestic. I usually stay in Crowne Plaza hotels which are rated 4* and I found the Majestic to be sadly lacking in the home comforts provided by lesser graded hotels, e.g. no tea/coffee making facilities in room and when I tried to order a coffee from room service, I was told it would take 20 mins!! Newspapers not available in lobby, although there was a machine (satellite kiosk) whereby you install your credit card and choose your newspaper. This puzzled me as having taken heed of the guidebooks, I stored my credit cards in my room safe, was I supposed to return to my room for my card, buy my paper, and then back to my room to store my card? Very cheap for a 5*. Breakfast was a hefty 24 euro each, so I was quite pleased to read about the complimentary coffee available in the hotel lobby for guests not wanting to take full american brekkie. That was until I read it was only available between 6 and 7am, after that you paid!!!! We did enjoy a meal in the restaurant of the hotel (not the Drolma - 48euro for soup!!!!) and the service was good, not a bad price either, coming to 73euro for two. Wonderful art in the lobby of the hotel and nice reception staff and concierge but it was the little things that were lacking - a kind of penny pinching type feeling which you don't expect when you are paying 200 euro a night. All in all, I did enjoy Barcelona and the Majestic does have a prime location but I did expect more from a 5* and would definetly take a chance on booking a less expensive hotel now that I have visited this lovely city.  
<Date>Mar 4, 2005

<Author>lass=
<Content>Superb accommodation  Having just returned from a four night stay at the Majestic Hotel on the occasion of my husbands 60th Birthday. I must congratulate the whole Team at the Majestic Hotel for a most happy and memorable stay! On arrival we were greeted with a friendly smile and Welcome to the Majestic Hotel from both the Reception and Porter who showed us to our Junior Suite. The accommodation was superb with luxurious furnishings throughout. An extra large double bed (with single firm mattresses per person thus ensuring a most comfortable sleep with no sag at all in the middle which can happen!)Large Double doors opened into the lounge area with a comfy sofa and armchairs to relax in, a fully enquipped desk and even a cd player as well as two TVs (one in the bedroom). The modern chrome and cream marble bathroom had a seperate large walk in powerful Shower, and even more welcome, a jacuzzi bath which was devine after walking ones feet off seeing the amazing sights! Lovely complimentary toiletries were numerous including razor and mousse, touthpaste and brush, moisturiser, fluffy dressing gowns, slippers etc etc. The Suite was located overlooking the busy Avenue de Gracia with two small balconies, once the double glazing doors were closed it must have been the most quietest acommodation we have ever stayed in. Brilliant !On our second evening we returned to find an iced bottle of Cava sparkling wine, mineral water, and a delicious decorated arrangement of fresh fruit including Pineapple,strawberries,chinese gooseberries,passion fruit,grapes etc etc.What a lovely and most welcome gesture. The fruit and mineral water was even replaced on our 3rd night! Thats what I call service! The Majestic Hotel has a brilliant brilliant location, between two of the Gaudi Must see buildings, with a huge choice of restaurants and shops to wander by on the 10 minute stroll to the Ramblas. The Metro is just outside and also the Tourist Bus Stop for seeing all the sights is only a minute away. Details/info available from Reception (3 euro with the balance payable to the Bus Courier making it the same price as paying the Tourist Bus Courier)enabling you to preplan your sightseeing, rather that trying to figure it out on the bus. Excellent discount coupons too for museum entries etc make it the best way to sightsee)On our departure at 7.15am in the morning a swift check out together with a taxi supplied in seconds ensured a good start to our journey home.If you want a Hotel with that something special feel this really is the Hotel to choose. A Hotel with the Wow factor Can`t wait to go back, truly a memorable stay in a wonderful City! Thank you so so very much Bruno,and all the Team, on ensuring such a fabulous stay.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous hotel, perfect location My fianc茅 and I have just returned from a three-night stay at the Majestic and would thoroughly recommend this hotel to anyone. We booked a Superior room, which was situated on the side of the hotel. Our room overlooked residential apartments, which was fine, though we had hoped to be at the front of the hotel (I think these views are reserves for suites).The room itself was pleasant. With two single beds, table and chairs and a bureau there was still sufficient room. A television with Spanish and a few English spoken channels was provided. An electronic safe was also provided free of charge. The bathroom was very spacious and bright with the WC and walk in shower separated by doors on either side.The hotel is impressive in all areas, in particular the rooftop terrace. With the pool, bar and seating area situated here this is a great place to relax and take in the spectacular views of the city. The hotel is in a great location in the heart of the city, surrounded by designer shops and within walking distance (10 minutes) of Las Ramblas.We found the staff at the Majestic to be very attentive and feel that their first rate service simply adds to the grandeur of the hotel. All in all this is a superb establishment that certainly deserves its 5 star status. We will definitely be staying at the Majestic again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A huge disappointment - very poor value My wife and I recently stayed for thee nights at the Hotel Majestic - what a misnomer!We booked through Lastminute (efficient) and paid approximately 1,000 Euros for the three nights (breakfast not included - see below) for a superior room.The location, on the Paseo de Gracia, is superb, especially as we were doing the tourist bit - it is close to many sites, and to the metro and the Barcelona tour bus stops.After that, with the notable exception of the front-desk staff, who were extremely helpful, everything was downhill ..........The problems centred around the room itself, and the (in) competency of the staff and their (poor) attitude.I don't think we've ever paid so much for such a small, poorly equipped room.We had requested a King bed - we got two singles pushed together.The windows are tiny, and the bathroom not much bigger.Room cleaning was perfunctory at best.However, the biggest issue with the room was (lack of) air-conditioning. During our stay in Barcelona, it was relatively warm, exacerbated by the heating in the room being on full when we arrived. We turned this off but, during the whole of our stay, we could never get the room cool enough to sleep in comfortably. When we complained, we were told that the air-conditioning was turned off in the winter in favour of heating, and nothing could be done (remember, this is a 5* hotel).Opening the window was no good - not only was it too small to make much difference, the hotel's location meant that there was always traffic noise.We could just about have lived with the room, had the service been great ..........Four examples -- on our first night, we had booked a restaurant outside the hotel. We asked the concierge to hail us a taxi, which he did. We inadvertently forgot to tip him so, on our return, my wife specifically sought him out and did tip him, with apologies. Yet the next three times we asked the concierge staff to hail a taxi, they clearly and deliberately ignored us, such that we had to do it ourselves,- the bar staff in the main bar on the ground floor seemed obsessed by tips. Having had poor service the first night (waiting 25 minutes for a simple order of drinks), we did not tip the waiter - on succeeding nights, we simply could not get the waiters to pay any attention to us- as I said earlier, breakfast is not included. We tried the breakfast buffet in the basement (no windows). Everything about breakfast was chaotic and disorganised - it took several minues to get seated, and then an eternity to get the tea we had ordered which, when it arrived, was lukewarm. Hoping for better things with room service the next day, we were sorely disappointed - wrong order, food that was barely warm, and this time the tea was almost cold!! At over 20 euros, the cost for waht you get is exorbitant.- last straw - on departure, we had an early morning flight to catch at Barcelona airport, travelling through the rush hour. Fifteen minutes after requesting a porter, no-one had appeared, so I called again - a further ten minutes elapsed with no show. My wife and I gathered up our luggage, and headed downstairs. When we hit the lobby, I'm sure you can guess by now what happened ..... three porters, no less, wishing to help us to a taxi, and earn the magic tip - we declined despite their evident disapproval.My summary - despite its wonderful location, the facilities of this hotel represent vary poor value for money (suggest you try the Hotel des Arts) - by no stretch of the imagination do they equate to five star.This is exacerbated by the approach and attitude of the staff - with the notable exception of the front desk, they seem driven by one motive - a tip.I could and would not recommend this hotel to anyone.David Shaw

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Superb! Booked this hotel for my parents as a 60th birthday gift (Oct 04) and was initially dismayed by some of the mixed reviews. I voiced my concerns to the hotel director (Senor Chiaruttini) via email, who very promptly replied. He suggested that I use one of the hotel's Junior Suites which meant paying a modest upgrade, but these were the most recently upgraded rooms. Regardless of which room I might book, he assured me that my parents would not be disappointed. My parents are experienced five star hotel visitors, especially to spanish destinations and they raved that the Majestic is the BEST hotel they have ever stayed in. The room was out of this world, the public areas had a lovely atmosphere and very attentive friendly staff. Having found the hotel to be so much to their liking, they found that it was in a perfect location for the city: in the old quarter and Ramblas: right beside an Metro station ( it took 15 mins to get back to the hotel from Camp Nou after the Champions League match Barca v Celtic). My parents fully intend to revisit the city and will definitely stay at the Majestic.

<Author>Badseyexplorer
<Content>Excellent position, Extremely comfortable Just returned from three nights at the Majestic and it looked fantastic decked out in its Christmas lights festooned from its many balconies. Inside, its lobby, bar and corridors certainly all look five star and the staff are very attentive and professional. We opted for a classic double room using their 'three nights for the price of two' offer. Our room (on the fourth floor) was certainly not large (as I have read in other reviews) but it was perfectly usable with a nice marble tile-lined bathroom and a great balcony looking out on to the Carrer de Valencia with a view of the Passeig de Gracia. While not cavernous, the room was certainly clean, had a good bed, quality fittings and good laundry.We opted not to use the restaurants for either breakfast or dinner so I cannot comment on these - but with so much great stuff on your doorstep why would you want to limit yourself to a hotel meal?Regardless of the room size, there are two real clinchers for this hotel: Its location and its rooftop. The location is perfect. The Passeig de Gracia metro station is one block away and with three or four lines going through it, it's easy to get everywhere else. But nevermind that, if you're an achitecture fan (Gaudi in particular) you've got the Casa Batllo one block to the south, La Pedrera two blocks to the north and the Sagrada Familia about eight blocks west. The shops round there are seriously smart and upmarket, but the food and drink is fantastic and much of it is very reasonable. Good tapas bars are dotted throughout and I must give special mention to La Bodegueta (Rambla de Catalunya, 100). This is a basement bar which you could easily miss but which the locals do not - it's full of them. If you want to sample great, tasty, non-flashy tapas away from the trail, go here. Enjoy the great atmosphere and witness the friendly bar staff make seriously efficient use of a tiny room where bottles of everything are stacked up behind the customers and where those bottles are routinely thrown above the drinkers' head's to keep the bar going.Back to the hotel. The other great thing is the rooftop terrace. Thanks to the Majestic's great height in comparison to most other buildings around it, it offers fantastic views of the city in almost all directions. There is a small pool up there as well as a bar and it is open until 10pm each night. One set of lifts go up and open inside the covered bar area. However, if you take the ones that go from nearest the hotel front desk, as the doors open on the 10th floor, you are immediately outside and directly facing the Sagrada Familia in the distance - breathtaking.I would definitely recommend this hotel, especially if you can get in on one of their 'three nights for the price of two' offers which really make it good value.  
<Date>Dec 13, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Poor value This was our third trip to Barcelona, so with that in mind we decided to splash out. Was it value for money? I think not! Was the location great? Oh yes!!!I have mixed views on the majestic, the hotel room was small, We had booked a Superior room at a cost of 760euros for 3 nights so not exactly budget but certainly small, offering few room extras, poor view and 2 single beds.The rooms that face on to the main street with balcony, are an additional 170euros per night......!! so dont think when you book you will end up overlooking Barcelona city, you will instead be facing the appartments across the street.The service was poor, inparticular the restaraunt. I found the staff brash quite abrupt and slow to serve. I ordered coffee only to be served tea, complained, was served hot water instead before finally getting coffee. Wait for it......the waiter then poured the coffee into my cup which he had half filled with tea earlier is that quality or what?This level of service was a not a one of it seemed to migrate through to the cleaning staff. The location is fantastic but with so many other hotels offering more in terms of room size etc an extra 5 minute walk from another hotel is worth considering. Here is a wee tip for you as well.....to order 2 glasses of wine on the roof terrace is 12euros to order a bottle is 13euros!!!!!!!!! Work that one out. All that said we had a nice time but would not go back to the Majestic, best you make up your own mind.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Somewhat Dissapointing. We stayed at the Majestic for 10 nights in September, and overall we found it to be a reasonably pleasant hotel but certainly overpriced/overated. On arrival we found out that because of the length of our stay, we had been upgraded to a superior room at no extra cost. Although this seemed like a nice gesture, we found the room to be very dissapointing and of a lower standard than we would have expected from the basic room we had paid for. It was very small, and not very well equiped considering that it was in a 5* hotel - there wasn't even a trouser press! The biggest disappointment with our room was the poor and erratic nature of the maid service. Some days our room wasn't cleaned at all, other days it was half cleaned, on two occasions the cleaner took all the towels but didn't replace them, and although after I complained at the front desk, towels were sent up and reassurances given that it wouldn't happen again, the following day the cleaner took all the pillow cases and didn't replace them! The bathroom wasn't cleaned properly during our entire stay - the sticky label from a previous guests shampoo bottle was stuck to the outside of the bath when we arrived, and it was still there when we left! As we suspected that the bathroom wasn't being cleaned other than around the sink, we deliberately placed small lengths of cotton thread on the toilet and bidet to see if they got cleaned off - they didn't!! Another negative point was the roof terrace - although it had good views, the swimming pool up there was tiny and should really be described as a dip pool instead. The roof top bar closed very early as well, which was a shame as it would have been nice to sit up there in the evenings. The hotel piano bar, on the other hand, was certainly a plus point - very friendly and attentive staff, together with a nice ambience. Location wise as well, the hotel is perfect with plenty of tapas bars, and good eateries in the area. It's also quite close to some of Barcelona's tourist attractions etc. Having stayed at other hotels in Barcelona (This was our 8th trip to the city), our opinion of the Majestic is that it just isn't worth the money as there are much nicer places to stay that cost far less.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved it My partner and I have just returned from 4 nights at the Majestic. We obtained a great deal for a junior suite direct with the hotel. When we arrived at 2 pm our suite was not ready but the staff could not have been more apologetic. We were escorted to the bar/lounge and told to order a drink on the house. This suited us as we were planning on going straight for a drink anyway. All the while we were kept informed of the progress of our suite. We decided to have a light lunch while we were waiting, for which we were fully expecting to pay, but that also was on the house. We were then taken to our suite by the PR girl, and given her personal extension number to call if we needed anything more. The suite was delightful in every way, with a wonderful view over the Passeig de Gracia. All of the staff were extremely friendly and helpful, and the hotel is in one of the best areas and within walking distance of all the main attractions. We found the Ramblas area to be too noisy and tacky, and were very glad we hadn't stayed in that area.Overall a wonderful trip, and would thoroughly recommend staying at the Majestic.

<Author>buffgirl73
<Content>First Class I had read some of the reviews of the Majestic before going but after booking and was a little concerned. I had also heard from a couple of friends that the standard rooms were small, so we booked a Junior Suite and it was fantastic. The recent renovations seem to have benefited these rooms hugely. Excellent fixtures and fittings (apart from one of the slightly temperamental TVs in the bedroom!), down to the bathrobes and slippers. The service was discreet and yet incredibly attentive just as it should be. The district is fab if you like shopping and within walking distance to pretty much everywhere except the Olympic Port which we found overly touristy and pretty lacking in atmosphere. It's also quieter than around Las Ramblas but with plenty going on. The only downside to this hotel that we found was the room service. The menu after 11pm was pretty limited and the quality of the food was pretty poor (in relation to what you'd expect from a 5* hotel). A small thing really but I think it would help them gulf the gap that they been attempting between a 4* and 5* establishment. All in all it was a great stay for great value, the prices seem to be about 2/3rds the price of the other 5* in the City.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A disappointment in many ways The Majestic has a wonderful location at the Paseig Gracia avenue in the most fashionable district of Barcelona. The building in itself is a landmark, surrounded by famous buildings, some by Gaudi himself. But - in a way I found they have damaged their position on the celebrated street. The ground floor of the hotel has been rented or sold to high fashion stores, so not much remains of the common area of the hotel except the reception and the bar - giving the impression of a narrow corridor. The hotel has two restaurants, one in a low basement, the other, more expensive, on the second floor - in spaces that are rather crammed.We decided on dinner in the cheaper restaurant, in the basement. This was one of the worst restaurant experiences I麓ve ever had. We had to ask three times for water. No bread arrived on the table. At long last I got the hors d'ouvre, a mediocre gaspachio. After one and an half hour the main course had not arrived. Then we decided to revolt and left. Other guests in the restaurant almost applauded us as we did so. The hotel staff had the good sense not to bill us for this nonexistant meal. We had some lovely tapas in a great place across the street, with very efficient service.More complaints. I asked for our bags to be sent down from our rooms, which is normal procedure in a five star establishment. They had not arrived in 45 minutes, despite my having repeated the request, so I went and got them myself.The room was rather small, but admittedly the bed was comfortable. Most of the hotel staff were also quite nice, exepting the wooden waiters in the restaurant.

<Author>efaa
<Content>Great Location and Charming Hotel I read all of the reviews on this site before we booked our hotel and was a little worried about the negative reviews about the Majestic, but we booked the Majestic anyway because we did not want to spend the extra money on either the Meridian or the Arts, the other two we were considering. When we got to the hotel, there was a problem with our room and they immediately upgraded us to a room with a huge balcony overlooking Pacia de Gracia. The location of the hotel is incredible and I liked it better then the location of the Meridian which is on the Ramblas, which, although a fun area, is very loud and does not have as many nice shops or restaurant that are on Pacia de Gracia. The Majestic is located across the street from the train station and most importantly to all of the architectural buildings created by Gaudi. The staff was very very friendly. I would especially recommend getting suggestions for restaurants from Shoshanna at the front desk, who was never wrong with her recommendations. The bar lounge was also a great area to go late night and get some Champaign. We usually stay in five star hotels when we travel, and we saved a significant amount of money staying at the Majestic over the Hotel Arts and were very very happy, especially since we were celebrating our anniversary. We would both recommend this hotel to any of our friends or family!Some other pointers for your traveling needs: For our anniversary my husband and I went to La Doma to eat, which I would recommend over and over and over again, so if celebrating a special occasion, this is the place to go! My other recommendation would be to take the tour bus around the city because the first couple of days my husband and I were taking the train and taxis to all the sites we wanted to see, as we began to realize that this tour bus runs from 8 am till 9 pm and drops you off everywhere so that you can get on and off and not worry about how to get to different places around Barcelona. The other place that we feel is a must was the Dali museum, an absolutely amazing place built by the artist himself. We took the train and it was very easy. Lastly, be careful of the restaurants located directly along La Rambla, we stopped at two different places for tapas and the food and even the sangrias were absolutely horrible both times! A major tourist trap!

<Content>Great Room, Great Service, Worth the Price My wife and I stayed at Hotel Majestice on the last day of our honeymoon. Although the rooms at the Hotel Majestic are a little pricey, it was well worth the money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A hotel that needs more attention to detail. This is a man's hotel, and not women friendly. The city's most expensive restaurant reeks of cigars, and the rooms need to be aired out. Small details like bathrobes that are soft and comfortable, kleenex in the room, plugs for laptops in the desks, alarm clocks, doors that do not slam shut with incredible noise, and sound-proofing would be useful. As well, the water supply of the city of Barcelona requires visitors to have spring water, this was not provided or even easily available. Heating and air-conditioning are very uneven and cannot be controlled.The pool on the roof is laughable - it is exactly 12 feet by six feet and unheated. They should simply put whirlpool jets in it and accept the fact that it is nothing more than a big bathtub. The roof also is unsafe for children as it has no safety rails and a very large drop down. While the staff of this hotel are very nice, the lack of attention to detail means this is no more than a businessman's hotel for very short stays, and the fact that at least half the rooms have a terrible view of a concrete carpark is another consideration. Breakfast is not included, is eaten in the basement and is 26 Euros. There are no no-smoking areas in the hotel.
